قوله : (والجواب بلا إله إلا الله) أي يفسدها عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكون مفسداً لأنه ثناء بصيغته فلا يتغير بعزيمته . ولهما أنه أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب وهو يحتمله فيجعل جواباً كتشميت العاطس وليس مقصود المصنف خصوص الجواب بهذه الكلمة هي ذكر أو قرآن قصد بها الجواب فهي على الخلاف كما إذا أخبر بخبر يسره فقال الحمد لله، أو بأمر عجيب فقال سبحان الله . ثم نص المشايخ على أشياء موجبه للفساد باتفاقهم وهو ما لو كان بين يدي المصلي كتاب موضوع وعنده رجل اسمه يحيى فقال يا يحيى خذ الكتاب بقوة [مريم: ١٢] أو رجل اسمه موسى وبيده عصا فقال له وما تلك بيمينك يا موسى [طه: ۱۷] أو كان في السفينة وابنه خارجها فقال يا بني اركب معنا [هود : ٤٢] أو طرق عليه الباب أو نودي من خارجه فقال ومن دخله كان آمناً [آل عمران : ٩٧] وأراد بهذا الألفاظ الخطاب لأنه لا يشكل على أحد أنه متلكم لا قارئ وهي مؤيدة لما قالاه واردة على أبي يوسف، ومما أورد على أبي يوسف الفتح على غير إمامه فإنه مفسد عنده وهو قرآن . كذا في فتح القدير. وأجاب عنه في غاية البيان بأن الفساد عنده فيه لأمر آخر وهو التعليم والإيراد مدفوع من أصله لأن أبا يوسف لا يقول بالفساد بالفتح على غير إمامه كما ذكره الزيلعي يكون على غير إمامه. قوله : (وفي القنية ارتج على الإمام إلى قوله (وتذكر ) أقول : يحتمل أن يكون المراد أنه تذكر بسبب الفتح وأن يكون تذكر بنفسه ولكنه صادف تذكره وفتح من ليس في صلاته في وقت واحد والظاهر الأول، لأنه لو كان تذكره من نفسه لا يظهر فرق بين أخذه في التلاوة قبل تمام الفتح أو بعده، ولا يظهر وجه الفساد لأن الفساد ليس بمجرد الفتح وإنما هو بالأخذ بسبب الفتح، وإذا كان تذكره من نفسه لم يوجد الأخذ بسبب الفتح وكون الظاهر أنه أخذ بالفتح فيضاف إليه لا ما في الأمر لأن ذلك من الديانات لا من الأمور الراجعة إلى القضاء حتى يعتبر الظاهر، ويدل عليه ما مر من أنه لو فتح على غير إمامه قاصداً القراءة لا التعليم لا تفسد عند الكل ومن أنه لو سمع الأذان فقال مثل ما يقول المؤذن تفسد إن أراد الجواب وإلا فلا، ونحو ذلك مما اعتبر فيه ما في نفس الأمر لا الظاهر المتبادر هذا ما ظهر لي فليتأمل قوله : (وهي مؤيدة لما قالاه واردة على أبي يوسف) أقول : الظاهر أن الفساد بها عند أبي يوسف لا للتغير بالعزيمة بل لما فيه بخلاف ما قصد به الجواب وليس فيه خطاب والحاصل أنه فرق بين قصد الجواب وقصد الخطاب عبرة له مع نفسه من الخطاب ثم اختلف المشايخ فيما إذا أخبر بخبر يسوءه فاسترجع لذلك بأن قال إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون مريداً بذلك الجواب، وصحح في الهداية والكافي الفساد عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف . وقال بعض المشايخ: إنه مفسد اتفاقاً، ونسبه في غاية البيان إلى عامة المشايخ . وقال قاضيخان : إنه الظاهر. ولعل الفرق على قوله أن الاسترجاع لإظهار المصيبة وما شرعت الصلاة لأجله والتحميد لإظهار الشكر والصلاة شرعت لأجله . وحكم لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله كالاسترجاع هو في منية المصلي. وقدمنا أنه لو قالها لدفع الوسوسة لأمر الدنيا تفسد ولأمر الآخرة لا تفسد . ثم أطلق المصنف الجواب بلا إله إلا الله وقيده في الكافي في فتاوى قاضيخان أنه لو خير بخبر يهوله فقال لا إله إلا الله أو الله أكبر وأراد الجواب فسدت ومما ألحق بالجواب ما في المجتبي : لو سج أو هلل يريد زجراً عن فعل أو أمراً به فسدت عندهما. وقيد بالجواب لأن لو أراد به إعلامه أنه في الصلاة كما إذا استأذن على المصلي إنسان فسبح وأراد به إعلامه أنه في الصلاة لم يقطع صلاته، وكذا لو عرض للإمام شيء فسبح المأموم لا بأس به لأن المقصود به إصلاح الصلاة فسقط حكم الكلام عند الحاجة إلى الإصلاح. ولا يسبح للإمام إذا قام إلى الأخريين لأنه لا يجوز له الرجوع إذا كان إلى القيام أقرب فلم يكن التسبيح مفيداً . كذا البدائع. وينبغي فساد الصلاة به لأن القياس فسادها به عند قصد الإعلام، وإنما ترك للحديث الصحيح من نابه شيء في صلاته فليسبح (۱) فللحاجة لم يعمل بالقياس، فعند عدمها يبقى الأمر على أصل القياس . ثم رأيته في المجتبي قال : ولو قام إلى الثالثة في الظهر قبل أن يقعد فقال المقتدي سبحان الله قيل لا تفسد وعن الكرخي : تفسد عندهما اهـ. وقد قدمنا حكم ما في بما فيه أداة نداء أو أداة خطاب لأن قصد الخطاب بما فيه ذلك من كلام الناس فليس ذكراً بصيغته وإن وافقه في اللفظ بخلاف ما قصد به الجواب، ومنه ما لو استأذنه رجل من خارج الباب ليدخل عليه فقال ومن دخله كان آمنا [آل عمران ۹۷] فإنه بمنزلة خطابه بقوله «ادخل». والظاهر أن أبا حنيفة ومحمداً يقولان إن هذه الخطابات القرآنية لا تصير خطاباً للحاضر المخصوص إلا بالنية والنية لا تغير الصيغة الأصلية عندهما قوله : (ولعل الفرق على قوله الخ) لا يخفي أن فيه اعتبار العزيمة وقد مر أن أبا يوسف لا يغير الصيغة بها تأمل قوله : وقيد بالجواب لأنه الخ) لا يخفى أن الإفساد ليس منوطاً بأن يقصد بالكلام الجواب فقط ليكون من كلام الناس بل مناطه كما في الفتح كونه لفظاً أفيد به معنى ليس من أعمال الصلاة ا.هـ. ولذا فسدت بقوله يا يحيى . خذ الكتاب وما تلك بيمينك يا موسى و يا بني اركب معنا عند قصد الخطاب كما مر وبفتحه على غير
His saying: (And the response with 'la ilaha illa Allah' means it invalidates according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: it does not invalidate because it is praise in its form, so it is not changed by his intention. And for them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] that he brought out the speech in the manner of a response and it bears that, so it is made a response like the sneezing supplication. And the author's intention is not specifically the response with this word; it is dhikr or Quran intended as a response, so it follows the disagreement, like if he is told good news and says 'Alhamdulillah', or a wondrous matter and says 'Subhanallah'. Then the mashayikh stated things that cause invalidation by consensus: such as if there is a book before the praying person and there is a man named Yahya and he says 'O Yahya, take the book with strength' [19:12], or a man named Musa with a staff and he says 'And what is that in your right hand, O Musa' [20:17], or he is in a ship and his son is outside it and he says 'O my son, embark with us' [11:42], or someone knocks on his door or is called from outside and he says 'And whoever enters it will be safe' [3:97], intending by these expressions address (khitab), because it is not unclear to anyone that he is a speaker, not a reciter. And this supports what they said and is a refutation of Abu Yusuf. And from what is refuted against Abu Yusuf: prompting (fath) other than his imam, for it invalidates according to him and it is Quran. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And he answered it in Ghayat al-Bayan that invalidation according to him is for another reason, which is teaching, and the objection is fundamentally rejected because Abu Yusuf does not hold invalidation by prompting other than his imam, as mentioned by al-Zayla'i. His saying: (And in al-Qunya: the imam stumbled and one not in his prayer prompted him and he remembered...) I say: It is possible that the meaning is that he remembered due to the prompting, and that he remembered by himself but his remembering coincided with the prompting of one not in his prayer at the same time, and the apparent is the first, because if his remembering was by himself there would be no difference between his beginning recitation before completing the prompting or after, and the ground of invalidation would not appear because invalidation is not merely by prompting but rather by reciting due to the prompting. And if his remembering was by himself, there was no reciting due to the prompting. And that the apparent is that he recited due to the prompting, so it is attributed to it, not what is in the matter, because this is from religious matters, not from matters returning to the judiciary so that the apparent is considered. And it is indicated by what passed: if he prompted other than his imam intending recitation, not teaching, it does not invalidate according to all; and if he heard the adhan and said like what the muadhdhin says, it invalidates if he intended response, otherwise no. And similar cases where what is in the inner reality is considered, not the apparent. This is what appeared to me, so let it be considered. His saying: (And it supports what they said and is a refutation of Abu Yusuf) I say: The apparent is that invalidation by it according to Abu Yusuf is not due to change by intention but rather because it is contrary to what is intended as a response and it does not contain address (khitab). The result is that he differentiated between intending response and intending address. A lesson for him with himself from the address. Then the mashayikh differed regarding when he is told bad news and makes istirja' by saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' intending it as a response. It is validated in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi that it invalidates according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. And some mashayikh said it invalidates unanimously, and it is attributed in Ghayat al-Bayan to most mashayikh. And Qadikhan said it is the apparent. Perhaps the difference according to him is that istirja' is for showing calamity, and prayer was not legislated for it, while tahmid is for showing gratitude, and prayer was legislated for it. And the ruling of 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' is like istirja', as in Munyat al-Musalli. And we mentioned that if he says it to repel waswasa for a worldly matter, it invalidates; for a matter of the Hereafter, it does not invalidate. Then the author absoluted the response with 'la ilaha illa Allah' and it is restricted in al-Kafi in Fatawa Qadikhan: if he is informed of a terrifying matter and says 'la ilaha illa Allah' or 'Allahu akbar' intending response, it invalidates. And from what is annexed to the response is what is in al-Mujtaba: if he says 'Subhan Allah' or 'la ilaha illa Allah' intending to rebuke an action or command it, it invalidates according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And it is restricted by response because if he intends by it to inform him that he is in prayer, like if a person seeks permission to enter upon the praying person and he says tasbih intending to inform him that he is in prayer, it does not break his prayer. Similarly, if something happens to the imam and the follower says tasbih, there is no harm because the purpose is to correct the prayer, so the ruling of speech falls due to need for correction. And he should not do tasbih for the imam when he stands for the second two rak'ahs because it is not permissible for him to return if he is closer to standing, so the tasbih is not beneficial. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And it should invalidate the prayer because analogy would invalidate it if intended for informing, but it is omitted due to the authentic hadith: 'Whoever is affected by something in his prayer should say tasbih' (1), so due to need analogy is not acted upon, so when there is no need, the matter remains on the original analogy. Then I saw in al-Mujtaba: if he stands for the third in Zuhr before sitting and the follower says 'Subhan Allah', it is said it does not invalidate, and from al-Karkhi: it invalidates according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And we have already given the ruling of what is in what contains a call particle or address particle because intending address with what contains that is from people's speech, so it is not dhikr in its form even if it agrees in wording, unlike what is intended as a response. Examples: if a man from outside the door seeks permission to enter upon him and he says 'And whoever enters it will be safe' [3:97], it is like addressing him by saying 'Enter'. And the apparent is that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say that these Quranic addresses do not become addressed to the specific person present except by intention, and intention does not change the original form according to them. His saying: (Perhaps the difference according to his saying, etc.) It is not hidden that it involves considering intention and it has passed that Abu Yusuf does not change the form by it. Reflect. His saying: (And it is restricted by response because, etc.) It is not hidden that invalidation is not dependent on intending by the speech a response only to be from people's speech, rather its basis as in al-Fath is that it is a word by which a meaning is conveyed that is not from the actions of prayer. End quote. Hence it invalidates by his saying 'O Yahya, take the book', 'And what is that in your right hand, O Musa', and 'O my son, embark with us' when addressing is intended, as passed, and by his prompting other than his imam.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling when a person in prayer says 'la ilaha illa Allah' intending it as a response to something. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it invalidates the prayer, while Abu Yusuf says it does not. The reasoning is that for Abu Yusuf, the phrase is inherently praise (thana') in its wording, and mere intention (niyya) does not change its essential form. For Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, by saying it as a response, the person is using it as speech (kalam) rather than dhikr, similar to replying to a sneeze with 'yarhamukallah' which would invalidate prayer. The passage then lists examples where there is consensus on invalidation: quoting Quranic verses with call particles (e.g., 'Ya Yahya', 'Ya Musa') intending to address a specific person, rather than recitation. This supports Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. It also discusses istirja' (saying 'Inna lillah...') when hearing bad news, and the rulings on tasbih for alerting. The key principle is that if the person intends address (khitab) or response (jawab) with words that are not normally used in prayer, even if they are Quranic, the prayer is invalidated. The commentator also distinguishes between tasbih for correcting the prayer (permissible) and for other purposes (invalidates).

Key Terms
الجواب (al-jawab): The act of responding to an external statement or event by uttering a phrase while in prayer.
الفتح (al-fath): Prompting or correcting the imam's recitation by saying the correct words.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Saying 'Subhan Allah' as a means of alerting or correcting in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a person in prayer hears good news and says 'Alhamdulillah' intending a response, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because it was said as a response.
B) The prayer remains valid because 'Alhamdulillah' is dhikr.
C) The prayer becomes makruh but not invalid.
D) The person must perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
In prayer, the intention behind an utterance determines whether it is valid dhikr or invalidating speech; responding to external events with even Quranic phrases can nullify the prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

When Dhikr Becomes Speech: Uttering La Ilaha Illallah in Prayer
Ruling on uttering La ilaha illallah or Allahu Akbar when shocked in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on uttering dhikr phrases during prayer when intended as a response or rebuke, and identify the correct application.

Core Idea
Any dhikr uttered as a response or rebuke in prayer becomes speech (kalam) and nullifies the prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: saying 'La ilaha illallah' in prayer. The general rule is that any utterance intended as an answer to external events or as a command/rebuke nullifies prayer, even if the words are normally considered dhikr. We will examine the precise conditions and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The author states that uttering 'La ilaha illallah' as a response (jawab) nullifies prayer. This is a general ruling. Note that the ruling is fasid (invalidates) the prayer.
The base matn by al-Kanz gives an unqualified ruling.
2
Apply the restriction from Qadikhan
Qadikhan restricts the ruling to cases where the person intends the utterance as an answer to shocking news. The phrase 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Allahu Akbar' nullifies only when intended as an answer.
Intention (niyyah) is key: is it dhikr or answer?
3
Extend to rebuke and command
Al-Mujtaba adds that saying 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah' to rebuke or command an action also nullifies, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This shows the illah (effective cause) is the intent of communication, not the specific words.
4
Distinguish from permissible tasbih
The exception is tasbih for informing others that one is in prayer (e.g., to gain entry), which is permitted due to necessity. This is not considered kalam.
This exception is mentioned elsewhere in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أطلق المصنف الجواب بلا إله إلا الله وقيده في الكافي في فتاوى قاضيخان أنه لو خير بخبر يهوله فقال لا إله إلا الله أو الله أكبر وأراد الجواب فسدت ومما ألحق بالجواب ما في المجتبي : لو سج أو هلل يريد زجراً عن فعل أو أمراً به فسدت عندهما.
Then the author (al-Kanz) stated the answer unconditionally with 'La ilaha illallah', but in al-Kafi in the Fatawa of Qadikhan it is restricted: if he is informed of a shocking news and says 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Allahu Akbar' intending the answer, it nullifies. And from what is attached to the answer is what is in al-Mujtaba: if he says Subhanallah or La ilaha illallah intending to rebuke an action or command it, it nullifies according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses two rulings: First, the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq ruled absolutely that saying 'La ilaha illallah' as an answer nullifies prayer. Qadikhan's Fatawa restrict this to cases where the person says 'La ilaha illallah' or 'Allahu Akbar' upon hearing shocking news with the intention of answering—then it nullifies. Second, from al-Mujtaba, if the person says 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah' intending to rebuke someone's action (like stopping a worldly wrong) or to command an action, it nullifies according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This emphasizes that any phrase, even if normally dhikr, becomes speech (kalam) when used as an answer or command, thus nullifying prayer. The exception is when the purpose is to inform about being in prayer (like tasbih for istidhan) which is permitted due to necessity.

Key Terms
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Saying 'Subhanallah' (glory be to Allah). In this context, using tasbih to rebuke or command an action in prayer.
الجواب (al-jawab): Responding to external speech or events with a phrase intended as an answer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Fatawa of Qadikhan, what is the ruling if a person in prayer hears shocking news and says 'La ilaha illallah' intending to answer?
A) It does not nullify because it is dhikr.
B) It nullifies the prayer.
C) It is valid if said softly.
D) It is valid only if said without intention.

Key Takeaway
A dhikr phrase uttered in prayer nullifies the prayer when intended as a response, rebuke, or command, because it becomes speech (kalam).

Rulings on Utterances During Prayer: Responses and Dhikr
Rulings on responses and dhikr during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on various utterances during prayer and identify which conditions make an utterance invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Dhikr during prayer is permissible but makruh; only speech intended as human conversation invalidates.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that clarifies what a praying person may say without invalidating their prayer. Many Muslims assume that any utterance breaks the prayer, but the Hanafi school distinguishes between dhikr (remembrance of Allah) and ordinary human speech. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary repeat of prayers and deepens your grasp of the school's approach to ritual purity in the act of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Utterances and Their Rulings
Read the text to list the various utterances mentioned: responding to adhan, salawat, cursing Shaytan, saying 'Sadaqallah', 'Amin', 'Labbaik', 'Allahu Akbar' during Tashriq, etc. For each, note whether the passage says it invalidates or not.
The default ruling is non-invalidation unless explicitly stated.
2
Distinguish Between Dhikr and Human Speech
The key principle is whether the utterance is a form of dhikr (worship) or a response to human conversation. Utterances like 'Alhamdulillah' for good news or 'Inna lillah' for bad news are problematic because they are conversational, but the soundest view still considers them dhikr.
Intention matters: if one intends to worship, it is dhikr; if to reply, it is speech.
3
Analyze the Conditions for Invalidation
The text specifies conditions that make an utterance invalidate: e.g., intending the adhan (full phrases) or habitually saying 'na'am' (yes). Imam Abu Yusuf differs on when adhan invalidates. List these conditions.
The later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirun) hold a stricter view on 'Amin' and 'Sadaqallah'.
4
Evaluate the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Notice the disagreement between the well-known (mashhur) position and the opinion in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. The author notes that the soundest opinion (al-asahh) is non-invalidation, though it contradicts the mashhur.
This exemplifies how later fatwa works can refine earlier positions.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi Today
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the listed utterances do not invalidate the prayer, though they are makruh tanzihi. Use this to advise someone who accidentally responded to an adhan during prayer.
The presence of ikhtilaf means a fatwa can adopt either view, but the majority follows non-invalidation.

كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها

إذا أجاب المؤذن أو صلى على النبي . ولو لعن الشيطان في الصلاة عند قراءة ذكره لا تفسد. وفي الخانية والظهيرية : ولو قرأ الإمام آية الترغيب أو الترهيب فقال المقتدي صدق الله وبلغت رسله فقد أساء ولا تفسد صلاته .اهـ. وهو مشكل لأنه جواب لإمامه، ولهذا قال في المبتغى بالمعجمة ولو سمع المصلي من مصل آخر ولا الضالين [الفاتحة: ٧] فقال آمين لا تفسد، وقيل تفسد وعليه المتأخرون وكذا بقوله عند ختم الإمام قراءته صدق الله وصدق الرسول اهـ. وفي المجتبى ولو لبى الحاج تفسد صلاته . ولو قال المصلي في أيام التشريق الله أكبر لا تفسد، ولو أذن في الصلاة وأراد به الأذان فسدت صلاته. وقال أبو يوسف : لا تفسد حتى يقول حي على الصلاة حي على الفلاح ولو جرى على لسانه نعم إن كان هذا الرجل يعتاد في كلامه نعم تفسد صلاته، وإن لم يكن عادة له لا تفسد لأن هذه الكلمة في القرآن فتجعل منه . ثم اعلم أنه وقع في المجتبي وقيل لا تفسد في قولهم أي لا تفسد الصلاة بشيء من الأذكار المتقدمة إذا قصد بها الجواب في قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، ولا يخفى أنه خلاف المشهور المنقول متوناً وشروحاً وفتاوي، لكن ذكر في الفتاوي الظهيرية في بعض المواضع أنه لو أجاب بالقول بأن يخبر بخبر يسره فقال «الحمد لله رب العالمين أو بخبر يسوءه فقال «إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون» تفسد صلاته والأصح أنه لا تفسد صلاته .اهـ. وهو تصحيح مخالف للمشهور .
Book of Prayer, Chapter on What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked Therein. If he responds to the mu'adhdhin or sends salawat upon the Prophet (PBUH). Even if he curses Shaytan in prayer while reciting his mention, it does not invalidate. In al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya: If the imam recites a verse of encouragement or deterrent and the follower says 'Sadaqallah and ballaghat rusuluh', he has done wrong and his prayer is not invalidated. It is problematic because it is a response to his imam. For this reason, he said in al-Mubtagha (with a 'ayn?) that if the praying person hears from another praying person 'wa la al-dallin' (Fatiha:7) and says 'Amin', it does not invalidate, and it is said it invalidates, and the later scholars hold that. Similarly, his saying at the completion of the imam's recitation 'Sadaqallah and Sadaq al-rasul'. In al-Mujtaba: If a pilgrim says 'Labbaik', his prayer invalidates. If the praying person says 'Allahu Akbar' during the days of Tashriq, it does not invalidate. If he calls the adhan in prayer intending the adhan, his prayer becomes invalid. Abu Yusuf said: It does not invalidate until he says 'Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah'. If the word 'na'am' runs on his tongue—if this man habitually uses 'na'am' in his speech, his prayer is invalidated; if it is not his habit, it does not invalidate because this word is in the Quran, so it is considered from it. Then know that it occurs in al-Mujtaba: 'And it is said they do not invalidate'—i.e., prayer is not invalidated by any of the aforementioned dhikr when one intends them as a reply, according to Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And it is not hidden that this is contrary to the well-known (mashhur) transmitted in matns, commentaries, and fatwas. But it is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya in some places that if he replies by speaking—reporting news that pleases him, saying 'Alhamdulillah rabb al-'alamin', or news that displeases him, saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un'—his prayer invalidates, and the soundest is that his prayer does not invalidate. This is a correction contrary to the mashhur.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling on various utterances that a praying person may make. The author examines whether such utterances invalidate the prayer. The general principle is that if a person responds to a mu'adhdhin, sends salawat upon the Prophet, or curses Shaytan during the recitation of a verse mentioning him, the prayer is not invalidated because these are forms of dhikr. However, if the intention is to respond to someone, it may be problematic. The text then discusses cases where the imam recites a verse of encouragement or warning and the follower says 'Sadaqallah wa ballaghat rusuluh' — this is considered improper (asa'a) but does not invalidate the prayer. There is an issue because it is a response to the imam. Similarly, saying 'Amin' after hearing another's recitation, or saying 'Sadaqallah' after the imam finishes recitation, is debated: some later scholars deem it invalidating. The text also notes that saying 'Labbaik' during Hajj invalidates prayer, while saying 'Allahu Akbar' during Tashriq days does not. A key distinction is made regarding the word 'na'am' (yes): if a person habitually uses it, it invalidates; otherwise, it is considered Quranic and thus not invalidating. The discussion concludes with a note from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that if one responds to news with 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Inna lillah', the soundest opinion is that prayer is not invalidated, though this contradicts the well-known position.

Key Terms
إجابة المؤذن (ijabat al-mu'adhdhin): Responding verbally to the call to prayer during one's own prayer
ذكر (dhikr): Any utterance of remembrance of Allah, including salawat and tasbih
جواب (jawab): A verbal response directed at another person during prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person says 'آمين' after hearing another's recitation of 'ولا الضالين' during prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer does not become invalid.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Utterances of dhikr, including responding to adhan and saying Amin, do not invalidate Hanafi prayer, though they are makruh; only speech intended as human conversation invalidates.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Saying and Replying to Salam During Prayer
Detailed analysis of salam during prayer: intentional vs. forgetful, to whom addressed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying salam during prayer, distinguish between salam addressed to a person and salam for exiting, and apply the rule that gestures do not invalidate.

Core Idea
Salam to a present person invalidates prayer always; salam to exit only if intentional.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq untangles a critical nuance in Hanafi fiqh: the utterance of 'salam' during prayer is not a single category. The author reconciles conflicting statements by distinguishing between the addressee—whether a present person or the intention to exit. Understanding this distinction prevents a common error: assuming all salam utterances are equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The utterance of 'السلام' (salam) during prayer, both initiating and responding. The overall ruling is that it invalidates prayer (mufsid).
The author emphasizes that salam is 'kalam al-nas' (speech of people), not dhikr.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on the principle that any speech during prayer invalidates, and salam is speech. The author cites the kaf al-khitab (addressing someone) as evidence that salam is communique, not dhikr.
The hadith about forbidding speech in prayer is the underlying source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'salam' when addressed to a person (e.g., using 'alaykum' or even without) indicates speech, not remembrance. The kaf of address makes it communique, thus invalidating.
Forgetfulness does not change the nature of the utterance as speech.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Hidayah) hold that salam forgetfully is considered dhikr and does not invalidate. The author refutes this by showing that the address element remains.
Intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author prefers the view that salam to a present person invalidates absolutely, citing al-Bada'i' and others. The mufta bihi position: salam to a person invalidates whether intentional or forgetful; salam as taslim invalidates only if intentional.
Gestures do not invalidate, as they are not speech.

His statement (i.e., the author's): '(and as-salam) (and its reply)' because it is from the speech of people. He made it absolute, so it includes intentional and unintentional, as stated in al-Khulasa. It also includes when he says 'as-salam' only without saying 'alaykum', as also in al-Khulasa. In al-Hidayah, there is what contradicts it, for he said: contrary to salam forgetfully, because it is from the dhikr, so it is considered dhikr in the state of forgetfulness and speech in the state of intentionality due to the presence of the kaf of address. And the commentators followed him. Similarly, Sadr al-Shari'ah conditioned salam to intentionality and did not condition the reply with it. Al-Shumunni said: Because replying to salam invalidates whether intentionally or forgetfully, because replying... The author (of al-Bahr) from this his imam and the like of that which has no answer, so the author's mention of 'jawaab' is not a precautionary restriction based on what he presented that the intent is not specifically the words 'la ilaha illa Allah' but every dhikr. Yes, if the specific word is intended, it is correct that it is precautionary regarding when one intends notification, and it does not invalidate due to the hadith that will come, as in al-Fath. His statement: (Then I saw it in al-Mujtaba, he said...). He said in al-Nahr: I say: It appears that this difference has a connection to another issue, that is if he returns while he was nearer to standing, then regarding his prayer's invalidation there is a difference, and if it is not invalidated, then it is beneficial. That is, on the opinion of non-invalidation, the tasbih is beneficial. It will come in the chapter on forgetfulness that the author corrects the opinion of non-invalidation and that it is the truth. So what he investigates here is based on what contradicts what he will verify. But it may be said: The claim of its benefit on the opinion of non-invalidation is prevented, because on both opinions he is prevented from returning, because he who says non-invalidation does not say that it is better to return to be beneficial. How, and in it is abandoning the obligation for something other than its type after having engaged in it. Ponder his statement: (And it is problematic because it is a reply to his imam). Some virtuous people said: This is derived from what is said that if a sneezer or hearer says 'Alhamdulillah', it does not invalidate, and if he intends the reply, then there is no meaning to its being problematic. Reflect. His statement: (And it has become clear to me that the meaning of salam is...). Completed the book of prayer, chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it, prayer. As-salam is not from the dhikr, rather it is speech and address, and speech invalidates absolutely. Thus, salam is conditioned to intentionality in al-Majma', and I have not seen anyone reconciling the expressions. It has become clear to me that the meaning of salam that invalidates absolutely is when it is to a present addressee; then there is no difference between intentional and unintentional (i.e., forgetfulness of being in prayer). And that the meaning of salam that invalidates only in the state of intentionality is when the addressee is not present, as they said: If he says salam after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully, his prayer does not invalidate. Similarly, if a latecomer says salam with the imam. Then after that I saw explicit statement in al-Bada'i' that salam to a person invalidates absolutely, and as for salam which is exiting from the prayer, it invalidates if intentional. And Allah is the granter of success. In al-Qunya: A person standing said salam thinking he had completed the prayer, then he knew he had not; it invalidates, and it is said he builds on it because he said salam in its wrong place, contrary to sitting and praying over a janazah. It is restricted to their absolute statement to when the salam is in the state of sitting. In it: A latecomer said salam forgetfully and made a supplication that was his habit; he repeats (the prayer). If he said 'Astaghfirullah' while it is his habit, he does not repeat. If the latecomer after the tarwiha says 'Subhanallah' etc. as is customary, it is expected that it does not invalidate. If the latecomer recited al-Fatiha after the imam's salam to the needy (?) forgetfully, it invalidates. Then all this is when he says salam with his tongue. As for if he replies to salam with his head or hand or finger, his prayer does not invalidate. If a person asks the praying person for something and he gestures with his head, or it is said to him 'Is this good?' and he gestures with his head no or yes, his prayer does not invalidate. In al-Majma': If he replies to salam with his tongue or hand, it invalidates. It is astonishing that the scholar Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, despite his extensive knowledge, said: Some who are not from the school have attributed to Abu Hanifa that prayer is invalidated by replying with the hand, and he did not know that anyone from the school has transmitted invalidation in replying with the hand. Rather, they mention non-invalidation without citing any difference within the school. Rather, the explicit statement of al-Tahawi supports it, and the author's coupling of reply with salam is an indication that what is meant is the greeting salam, and there is no difference in this between intentional and unintentional, hence he made it absolute. His statement: (Then after that I saw the explicit statement in al-Bada'i'...). Similar to what is in al-Bada'i' in the commentary of al-Maqdisi from al-Zad where he said: In al-Haruniyyat, if a person standing says salam thinking he had completed, then he had not completed, it invalidates because he said salam in its wrong place, contrary to sitting and janazah prayer. If he says salam to a person forgetfully, saying 'as-salam' then he knows and remains silent, it invalidates. In al-Nahr: Then I saw in Zad al-Faqir by Ibn al-Humam a good statement. He said: Speech invalidates except salam forgetfully. This does not mean salam to a person, as they explicitly stated that if he says salam to a person forgetfully, saying 'as-salam' then he knows and remains silent, his prayer invalidates. Rather, the meaning is the salam for exiting the prayer forgetfully before completing it. The issue is that he thinks he has completed. As for if he says salam in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully after two rak'ahs thinking they are tarwiha and the like, his prayer invalidates. So retain this. His statement: (Because he said salam in its wrong place) is a reason for invalidation, not for the statement 'and it is said he builds on it' as apparent from the wording. Besides, the statement 'and it is said he builds on it' is not present in what I saw in al-Qunya. His statement: ( 'ala al-muhtaj') is as in al-Qunya. Consider its meaning. In some copies of al-Bahr, it is 'ala al-mu'tad', and in some, 'ala al-mukhtar'. His statement: (And this speaker) is the one referred to as 'ma'.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of what invalidates prayer, focusing on the utterance of 'السلام' (salam) and its reply. The author first explains that the matn's statement 'والسلام ورده' is general, covering both intentional and unintentional cases. There is a difference of opinion: some scholars distinguish between salam as dhikr (in forgetfulness) and as speech (when intentional). The author then presents a resolution: salam addressed to a present person invalidates prayer whether done intentionally or forgetfully, while salam intended as the final taslim to exit prayer only invalidates if done intentionally before completion. The text cites the Bada'i', al-Qunyah, and other sources to support this distinction. It also discusses cases like a latecomer (masbuq) saying salam forgetfully, or a person standing and saying salam thinking he has finished. The ruling on responding to salam with gestures only (head, hand, finger) is that it does not invalidate prayer, whereas responding verbally does. The passage ends with a comment by Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi criticizing an attribution to Abu Hanifa that responding with the hand invalidates prayer, asserting that the Hanafi position is that it does not.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): The phrase 'السلام عليكم' used to greet or to exit prayer (taslim).
رد السلام (radd al-salam): Responding to a greeting during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person is praying and someone greets him with salam, and he responds by nodding his head, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer does not become invalid.
C) The prayer is invalid only if he intended speech.
D) He must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Salam to a present person invalidates prayer regardless of intent; salam for exiting only invalidates if intentional; gestures never invalidate.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on Saying Salam (Greeting) During Prayer
Determining when salam invalidates prayer: intentional vs forgetful, addressed to present vs absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when saying salam during prayer invalidates the prayer according to the Hanafi school, distinguishing between intentional and forgetful contexts and the presence of the addressee.

Core Idea
Salam is speech, and speech invalidates prayer, but the ruling depends on intent and addressee.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that clarifies the Hanafi position on saying the greeting 'Assalamu alaykum' during salah. The author reconciles apparent contradictions in earlier texts by distinguishing two factors: whether the salam is addressed to a present or absent person, and whether it was said intentionally or forgetfully. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly assessing the validity of your prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that the Hanafi school classifies salam as speech (kalam), and any speech during prayer invalidates it absolutely.
This is the foundational rule from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Distinguish between greeting and exit salam
Note that the passage differentiates between the greeting salam (تحية) and the salam to exit prayer. Exit salam only invalidates if done intentionally.
The greeting salam has further distinctions.
3
Apply the presence condition
For the greeting salam, the key factor is whether the addressee is present. If present, the salam invalidates even if forgetful. If absent, only intentional salam invalidates.
The author supports this with the example of forgetfully saying salam after two rak'ahs.
4
Evaluate the masbuq exception
A latecomer (masbuq) who says salam with the imam is considered forgetful and the salam is to an 'absent' imam? Actually, it is treated as not invalidating because the intention is not to greet a person.
This reinforces the principle that salam to a present person is the critical element.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
السلام ليس من الأذكار بل هو كلام وخطاب والكلام مفسد مطلقاً .اهـ. وهكذا قيد السلام بالعمد في المجمع ولم أر من وفق بين العبارات، وقد ظهر لي أن المراد بالسلام المفسد مطلقاً أن يكون لمخاطب حاضر فهذا لا فرق فيه بين العمد والنسيان أي نسيان كونه في الصلاة، وأن المراد بالسلام المفسد حالة العمد فقط أن لا يكون المخاطب حاضر كما قالوا : لو سلم على رأس الركعتين في الرباعية ساهياً، فإن صلاته لا تفسد . وكذا لو سلم المسبوق مع الإمام . ثم بعد ذلك رأيت التصريح به في البدائع أن السلام على إنسان مبطل مطلقاً، وأما السلام وهو الخروج من الصلاة فإنه مفسد إن كان عمداً والله الموفق.
Chapter of what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. The greeting (salam) is not from the remembrances but is speech and address, and speech invalidates absolutely. End quote. Thus the greeting is restricted to intentional in al-Mujma' and I have not seen anyone reconciling the expressions. It has become apparent to me that what is meant by the greeting that invalidates absolutely is that it is for an addressee who is present, so there is no difference in this between intentional and forgetful, i.e., forgetting that he is in prayer. And that what is meant by the greeting that invalidates only in the case of intentional is when the addressee is not present, as they said: if he says salam after the head of two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully, his prayer is not invalidated. Similarly, if a latecomer says salam with the imam. Then after that I saw explicit statement about it in al-Bada'i': that the greeting to a human invalidates absolutely. As for the salam which is the exit from prayer, it is invalidating if intentional. And Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It clarifies the Hanafi position on saying salam (the greeting) during prayer. The core principle is that salam is considered speech (kalam), not dhikr, and speech invalidates prayer. However, the author reconciles apparent contradictions in earlier texts. He distinguishes two situations: (1) if the salam is addressed to a person who is present, it invalidates whether done intentionally or forgetfully; (2) if the addressee is not present, only intentional salam invalidates. He supports this with examples: forgetfully saying salam after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer does not invalidate, nor does a latecomer (masbuq) saying salam with the imam. He then cites from al-Bada'i' that salam to a human invalidates absolutely (meaning even if forgetful?). But the author clarifies that this applies only when the addressee is present. The salam for exiting prayer (tahiyyat al-salat) invalidates only if intentional. This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach: the ruling depends on the nature of the salam and the situation.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): Uttering the greeting 'Assalamu alaykum' or the exit salam during prayer. The passage distinguishes between greeting salam (تحية) and exit salam (الخروج من الصلاة).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person is in a four-rak'ah prayer and forgetfully says 'Assalamu alaykum' after two rak'ahs, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalidated because salam is speech.
B) The prayer is not invalidated because it was forgetful and the addressee is absent.
C) The prayer becomes makruh but remains valid.
D) It depends on the intention of the person.

Key Takeaway
Saying the greeting salam during prayer invalidates it even if forgetful when addressed to a present person; otherwise, only intentional salam invalidates.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Responding to Salam During Prayer and the Dispute About Gesture
Intra-Hanafi legal analysis of gesture response in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on responding to salam by gesture during prayer and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Responding to salam by gesture during prayer does not invalidate it, based on Prophetic practice.

This passage addresses a common scenario: someone greets you while you are praying. How should you respond? The Hanafi school, relying on hadith, holds that a gesture (head, hand, finger) does not invalidate your prayer, though some later Hanafis dissented. We'll examine the evidence and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what the act is (responding to salam by gesture) and the Hanafi ruling: it does not invalidate prayer, but it is makruh tanzihan.
The act is distinct from verbal response, which invalidates.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited: the Prophet (saw) responded by gesture while praying, as reported in Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi.
This shows permissibility despite general prohibition of speech.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some later Hanafi scholars argued that gesture invalidates by qiyas with a handshake intended as salam. Understand both sides.
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that it does not invalidate.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the mufta bihi, a person who responds by gesture does not need to repeat the prayer.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : سلم قائماً على ظن أنه أتم الصلاة ثم علم أنه لم فسدت، وقيل يبنى لأنه سلم في غير محله بخلاف القعود وصلاه الجنازة اهـ. وهو مقيد لإطلاقهم بما إذا كان السلام حالة القعود. وفيها : سلم المسبوق ساهياً ودعا بدعاء كان عادته أعاد، ولو قال استغفر الله وهو عادته لا يعيد . ولو قال المسبوق بعد الترويحة سبحان الله إلى آخره كما هو المعتاد ينبغي أن لا تفسد قرأ المسبوق الفاتحة بعد سلام الإمام على المحتاج ناسياً فسدت اهـ . ثم هذا كله إذا سلم أورد بلسانه، أما إذا رد السلام برأسه أو بيده أو بأصبعه لا تفسد صلاته، ولو طلب إنسان من المصلي شيئاً فأومأ برأسه أو قيل له أجيد هذا فأومأ برأسه بلا أو بنعم لا تفسد صلاته اهـ. وفي المجمع : لو رد السلام بلسانه أو بيده فسدت ومن العجب أن العلامة ابن أمير حاج الحلبي مع سعة إطلاعه قال : إن بعض من ليس من أهل المذهب قد عزا إلى أبي حنيفة أن الصلاة تفسد بالرد باليد وأنه لم يعرف أن أحداً من أهل المذهب نقل الفساد في رد السلام باليد وإنما يذكرون عدم الفساد من غير حكاية خلاف في المذهب فيه، بل وصريح كلام الطحاوي في يؤيده عطف المصنف الرد على السلام فإنه قرينة على أن المراد به سلام التحية، وهذا لا فرق فيه بين العمد والنسيان فلذا أطلقه قوله : (ثم بعد ذلك رأيت التصريح به في البدائع الخ) ومثل ما في البدائع في شرح العلامة المقدسي عن الزاد حيث قال : وفي الهارونيات لو سلم قائماً على ظن أنه أتم ثم أنه لم يتم تفسد لأنه سلم في غير محله بخلاف القعود وصلاة الجنازة، ولو سلم على إنسان ساهياً فقال السلام ثم علم فسكت تفسد ا.هـ. وفي النهر ثم رأيت في زاد الفقير للعلامة ابن الهمام كلاماً حسناً قال الكلام مفسد إلا السلام ساهياً، وليس معناه السلام على إنسان إذ صرحوا بأنه إذا سلم على إنسان ساهياً فقال السلام ثم علم فسكت تفسد صلاته، بل المراد السلام للخروج من الصلاة ساهياً قبل إتمامها ومعنى المسألة أن يظن أنه أكمل أما إذا سلم في الرباعية مثلاً ساهياً بعد ركعتين على ظن أنها ترويحة ونحو ذلك تفسد صلاته فليحفظ هذا ا هـ. قوله : (لأنه سلم في غير محله تعليل للفساد لا لقوله وقيل يبنى كما توهمه العبارة على أن قوله «وقيل يبنى» ليس موجوداً فيما رأيته في القنية قوله : ( على المحتاج كذا هو في القنية وانظر ما معناه، وفي بعض نسخ البحر على المعتاد وفي بعضها على المختار قوله : (وكان هذا القائل) وهو العبر عنه

الآثار يفيد أن . عدم الفساد قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد وكأن هذا القائل فهم من نفي
قال :
الرد بالإشارة الفساد على تقديره كما هو كذلك في الرد بالنطق لكن الثابت ما ذكرنا اهـ. فإن صاحب المجمع من أهل المذهب المتأخرين، والحق ما ذكره العلامة الحلبي أن الفساد ليس بثابت في المذهب وإنما استنبطه بعض المشايخ في فرع نقله من الظهيرية والخلاصة وغيرهما أنه لو صافح المصلي إنساناً بنية السلام فسدت صلاته. ونقل الزاهدي بعد نقله عن حسام الأئمة المودني أنه قال : فعلى هذا تفسد أيضاً إذا رد بالاشارة لأنه كالتسليم باليد وكذا ذكره البقالي وقال : عند أبي يوسف لا تفسد اهـ. ويدل لعدم كونه مفسداً ما ثبت في سنن أبي داود وصححه الترمذي عن ابن خرج النبي الله إلى قباء فصلى فيه قال فجاءته الأنصار فسلموا عليه وهو يصلي فقلت لبلال : كيف كان النبي يا ال اللي يرد السلام عليهم حين كانوا يسلمون عليه وهو يصلي؟ قال : يقول هكذا وبسط كفه وبسط جعفر بن عون كفه وجعل بطنه أسفل وجعل ظهره إلى فوق . وما عن صهيب : مررت برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو يصلي فسلمت عليه فرد علي إشارة ولا أعلمه قال الإشارة باصبعه . رواه أبو داود والترمذي وحسنة. فإن قلت : إنها تقضي عدم الكراهة وقد صرحوا كما في منية المصلي وغيرها بكراهة السلام على المصلي ورده بالإشارة أجاب العلامة الحلبي بأنها كراهة تنزيهة وفعله عليه السلام لها إنما كان تعلماً للجواز فلا يوصف بالكراهة، وقد أطال الكلام هنا إطالة حسنة كما هو دأبه . وحينئذ فيحتاج إلى الفرق بين المصافحة والرد باليد وقد علل
رحمه الله
ببعض من ليس من أهل المذهب فهم من نفي الرد بالإشارة الفساد أي فهم من قولهم ولا يرد بالإشارة أن المراد أنها تفسد على تقدير الرد بها كما أن الحكم كذلك في الرد بالنطق، فقوله «من نفي الرد مصدر مجرور بمن مضاف إلى مفعوله وقوله بالإشارة متعلق بالرد، وقوله الفساد بالنصب مفعول «فهم قوله : (فإن صاحب المجمع تعليل لقوله ومن العجب الخ» وقوله «والحق» حاصله إقرار العلامة الحلبي على أن الفساد ليس بثابث في المذهب بعد انتقاد قوله، وأنه لم يعرف أن أحداً من أهل المذهب نقل الفساد بأن صاحب المجمع نقله وهو من أهل المذهب وهذ منشأ العجب قوله : (فإن قلت إنها تقتضي عدم (الكراهة ذكر الشارح الزيلعي ما يمنع ذلك فإنه قال : ولا يرد بالإشارة لأنه عليه السلام لم يرد بالإشارة على ابن مسعود ولا على جابر، وما روي من قول صهيب «سلمت على النبي عليه السلام وهو يصلي فرد علي بالإشارة» يحتمل أنه كان نهياً له عن السلام أو كان في حالة التشهد وهو يشير فظنه رداً ا . وفي شرح العلامة المقدسي بعد ذكره الحاصل ما في شرح المنية أقول : وما ذكره الشارح رحمه الله تعالى يرد هذا لأن الرد مشترك یراد به عدم القبول ولعله المراد من فعله الله فكأنه يرد عليهم سلامهم ويعلمهم أنه في الصلاة ويراد به المكافأة على السلام الذي هو حق على المسلم لأخيه وليس هذا بمراد في هذا المقام، وبهذا التوفيق يستغنى عن التطويل والتعسف وجعله مكروهاً تنزيهاً لوقوعه من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ا هـ. وظاهر کلامه الميل إلى القول بالفساد ولكن لا يخفى أنه إذا قيل سلمت عليه فرد علي سلامي إنما يستعمل
اهـ.
And in al-Qunyah: He said salam while standing thinking he had completed prayer then he knew he had not, so it is invalidated, and it is said: he builds because he said salam in its wrong place contrary to sitting and funeral prayer. End quote. And it restricts their absolute statement to when the salam is in the sitting state. And in it: a latecomer said salam forgetfully and made a supplication that was his habit, he repeats; and if he said 'astaghfirullah' and that was his habit, he does not repeat. And if the latecomer after the tarwiha said 'subhanallah' etc. as is customary, it should not invalidate. The latecomer read al-Fatiha after the imam's salam to the needy forgetfully, so it invalidates. End quote. Then all this is if he says salam with his tongue. But if he responds to the greeting with his head or hand or finger, his prayer is not invalidated. And if a person asks the one in prayer for something and he gestures with his head, or he is told 'do this' and he gestures with his head with 'no' or 'yes', his prayer is not invalidated. End quote. And in al-Mujma': if he responds to the greeting with his tongue or hand, it is invalidated. And it is strange that the scholar Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi, with his vast knowledge, said: Some who are not of the madhhab attributed to Abu Hanifa that prayer is invalidated by responding with the hand, and he did not know that anyone from the madhhab transmitted invalidation in responding to the greeting with the hand; rather they mention no invalidation without reporting any disagreement in the madhhab about it. Rather the explicit statement of al-Tahawi supports it, that the author's joining the response to the greeting is an indication that what is meant is the greeting of salutation, and there is no difference in this between intentional and forgetful, so he stated it absolutely. He said: then after that I saw explicit statement about it in al-Bada'i' etc. And similar to what is in al-Bada'i' in the commentary of al-Maqdisi on al-Zad where he said: And in al-Haruniyyat: if he said salam while standing thinking he completed then he did not complete, it invalidates because he said salam in its wrong place contrary to sitting and funeral prayer. And if he said salam to a human forgetfully and said 'al-salam' then knew and kept silent, it invalidates. End quote. And in al-Nahr: then I saw in Zad al-Faqir by Ibn al-Humam a good statement: he said: speech invalidates except salam forgetfully. And its meaning is not salam to a human, for they explicitly stated that if he says salam to a human forgetfully and says 'al-salam' then knows and keeps silent, his prayer invalidates. Rather what is meant is the salam of exiting prayer forgetfully before its completion, and the meaning of the issue is that he thinks he completed. But if he says salam in a four-rak'ah prayer forgetfully after two rak'ahs thinking it is tarwiha and the like, his prayer invalidates. So memorize this. End quote. His statement: because he said salam in its wrong place is an explanation for invalidation, not for his saying 'it is said: he builds' as the expression suggests, for his saying 'and it is said: he builds' is not present in what I saw of al-Qunyah. His statement: 'to the needy' is how it is in al-Qunyah, and consider its meaning. And in some copies of al-Bahr 'on the customary' and in some 'on the chosen'. His statement: 'and this speaker' and he is the one who... [Page 15] ...al-Athar informs that non-invalidation is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. And it is as if this speaker understood from the negation of response by gesture the invalidation based on its supposition, just as it is so in response by speech, but what is established is what we mentioned. End quote. For the author of al-Mujma' is of the later scholars of the madhhab, and the truth is what al-Halabi mentioned: that invalidation is not established in the madhhab, rather some mashayikh deduced it in a branch transmitted from al-Zahiriyya and al-Khulasa and others: that if a person in prayer shakes hands with someone with the intention of salam, his prayer invalidates. And al-Zahidi transmitted after him from Hisam al-A'imma al-Mudani that he said: on this, it also invalidates if he responds by gesture, because it is like greeting with the hand. Similarly, al-Baqqali mentioned it and said: according to Abu Yusuf, it does not invalidate. End quote. And it proves that it is not invalidating what is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi from Ibn... that the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out to Quba and prayed there. He said: the Ansar came and greeted him while he was praying. I said to Bilal: how was the Prophet, O... he would respond to their greeting when they greeted him while he was praying? He said: he would do like this, and he spread his palm, and Ja'far ibn 'Awn spread his palm and placed its inner side down and its outer side up. And from Suhayb: I passed by the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was praying and I greeted him, and he responded to me by gesture, and I do not think he said 'gesture with his finger'. Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi and declared good. If you say: that implies non-dislike, and they have stated, as in Munyat al-Musalli and others, the dislike of greeting the one in prayer and responding by gesture. Al-Halabi answered that it is a tanzih dislike, and his (peace be upon him) doing it was only for teaching permissibility, so it is not described as disliked. And he has gone on at length here, a good length as is his custom. Then, the difference between handshake and response by hand is needed. And he commented: some who are not of the madhhab understood from the negation of response by gesture the invalidation, i.e., they understood from their statement 'and he does not respond by gesture' that it is intended that it invalidates on the assumption of responding by it, just as the ruling is likewise in response by speech. So his statement 'from the negation of response' is a gerund governed by 'min' added to its object, and his statement 'by gesture' is attached to 'response', and his statement 'the invalidation' is accusative as object of 'understood'. His statement: 'for the author of al-Mujma' is an explanation for his statement 'and it is strange etc.', and his statement 'and the truth' the summary is that al-Halabi affirms that invalidation is not established in the madhhab after criticizing his statement, and that he did not know that anyone from the madhhab transmitted invalidation, because the author of al-Mujma' transmitted it and he is of the madhhab, and this is the source of wonder. His statement: 'if you say that it implies non-dislike', the commentator Zayla'i mentioned what prevents that, for he said: and he does not respond by gesture because he (peace be upon him) did not respond by gesture to Ibn Mas'ud nor to Jabir. And what is narrated from Suhayb 'I greeted the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he was praying and he responded to me by gesture' could be that it was a prohibition for him from greeting, or that he was in the state of tashahhud and was gesturing, so he thought it a response. End quote. And in the commentary of al-Maqdisi after mentioning the summary of what is in Sharh al-Munya: I say: what the commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned refutes this, because 'response' is shared in meaning: it can mean non-acceptance, and perhaps that is what is meant by his action, as if he was replying to their greeting and informing them that he is in prayer; and it can mean reciprocation of the greeting which is a right of the Muslim upon his brother, and that is not intended in this place. And with this reconciliation, lengthy and forced explanations become unnecessary, and it is made disliked tanzihan because it occurred from the Prophet (peace be upon him). End quote. And his apparent speech leans towards the opinion of invalidation, but it is not hidden that when it is said 'I greeted him and he responded to my greeting' it is only used... End quote.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by citing rulings from al-Qunyah on various cases of salam during prayer (e.g., salam while standing thinking one has completed, latecomer cases). Then it transitions to the key issue: responding to a greeting by gesture (head, hand, finger) does not invalidate prayer. However, al-Mujma' states that responding by tongue or hand invalidates. The author expresses amazement at the scholar Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi who noted that some non-madhhab individuals attributed to Abu Hanifa the view that responding by hand invalidates, whereas the established Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that it does not. The author defends the majority view using hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi where the Prophet (saw) responded by gesture. The discussion includes a rebuttal of those who argue that gesture invalidates by analogy with a handshake intended as salam. The author also addresses the issue of dislike (karaha), concluding that it is only tanzih (disliked but not invalidating). The passage ends with commentary from al-Maqdisi leaning towards invalidation but the overall Hanafi position is upheld: gesture does not invalidate.

Key Terms
الرد بالإشارة (al-radd bi al-ishara): Responding to a greeting (salam) by a gesture such as nodding the head or moving the hand, as opposed to verbal response.
المصافحة (al-musafaha): Handshake. In this context, shaking hands with the intention of salam during prayer is considered invalidating by some, but the author distinguishes it from a simple gesture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect on prayer if a person responds to someone's greeting by gesturing with his hand while in salah?
A) The prayer is invalidated because any movement invalidates.
B) The prayer remains valid but the act is makruh tanzihan.
C) The prayer is invalidated because he intended to respond.
D) The prayer becomes batil and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Responding to salam by gesture during prayer is permissible and does not invalidate the prayer, based on the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the early Hanafi scholars.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Gestural Response During Prayer: Does It Invalidate?
Analysis of whether gestural response invalidates prayer, with intra-madhhab disagreement on shaking hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on responding to a greeting with a gesture during prayer, distinguish it from shaking hands, and evaluate the proofs and intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Responding to a greeting with a gesture does not invalidate prayer; shaking hands may if it involves excessive action.

Greeting someone who is praying is generally disliked, but what about responding? The Hanafi school distinguishes between verbal response (which invalidates) and gestural response (which does not). This lesson unpacks the evidence from hadith, the intra-madhhab dispute over shaking hands, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: gestural response does not invalidate prayer.
2
Identify the primary proof
Locate the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Suhayb showing the Prophet responded by gesture.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi; its transmission is zanni.
3
Examine the objection
Consider al-Zayla'i's attempt to interpret the hadith as indicating prohibition or that the Prophet was not actually responding.
Al-Zayla'i suggests the gesture was a prohibition, not a response.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand why the manifest meaning is preferred: context and usage indicate response, not prohibition.
The word 'radda' in the hadith typically means answering a greeting.
5
Distinguish shaking hands
Apply the criterion of 'amal kathir (excessive action): shaking hands may invalidate if it involves substantial movement, unlike a simple gesture.
This is the preferred view of al-Halabi and al-Nahr.

The traditions indicate that the position of non-invalidation is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. It is as if this speaker understood from the negation of responding by gesture the invalidity, i.e., he understood from their statement 'and he should not respond by gesture' that the intended meaning is that it invalidates when one does respond by it, just as the ruling is likewise in responding verbally. So his statement 'from the negation of responding' is a verbal noun governed by 'from' added to its object, and his statement 'by gesture' is related to 'the response', and his statement 'the invalidity' is in the accusative as the object of 'understood'. His statement: (for the author of al-Majma' is a reason for his statement 'and from the wondrous' etc.) And his statement 'the truth' is the purport of the endorsement of al-Allamah al-Halabi that invalidity is not established in the madhhab after criticizing his statement, and that he did not know that anyone from the people of the madhhab transmitted invalidity, since the author of al-Majma' transmitted it and he is from the people of the madhhab, and this is the source of wonder. His statement: (For if you say that it necessitates the absence of dislike) the commentator al-Zaylai mentioned what prevents that, for he said: And he should not respond by gesture because he (peace be upon him) did not respond by gesture to Ibn Mas'ud nor to Jabir, and what is narrated from Suhayb 'I greeted the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he was praying and he responded to me by gesture' is likely that it was a prohibition for him of greeting, or that he was in the state of tashahhud and was pointing, so he thought it was a response. And in the commentary of al-Allamah al-Maqdisi after mentioning the summary of what is in Sharh al-Munyah, I say: What the commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned contradicts this because 'response' is shared; it may mean non-acceptance, and perhaps that is the intended meaning of his action (peace be upon him), as if he was rejecting their greeting and teaching them that he is in prayer. And it may mean reciprocation for the greeting which is a right of a Muslim over his brother, and this is not intended in this context. With this reconciliation, there is no need for prolongation and artificiality, and making it disliked with tanzih because it occurred from the Prophet (peace be upon him). End. And the apparent meaning of his speech is inclination towards the opinion of invalidity, but it is not hidden that when one says 'I greeted him and he responded to my greeting', the word 'response' is used in the sense of answering the greeting by context and usage. If it were in the sense of non-acceptance and prohibition of greeting, it would be necessary to say 'he did not answer my greeting' or 'he did not accept' or 'he forbade me' and similar expressions that are not intended. Carrying the evidence on the most apparent is better, and other than that is artificial, not to be resorted to except with a compelling reason. His statement: (And it is objected to him that responding by gesture is meaningful speech. He said in al-Nahr: The better way is to attribute invalidation due to shaking hands to it being a lot of action, unlike responding by hand. End. And this is apparent from the words of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munyah. His statement: (Then know that it is disliked to greet the one praying, the reader, the one sitting for judgment or for study of fiqh or for relieving oneself, and if one greets them, it is not obligatory for them to respond because it is out of place. Thus mentioned the commentator. And it is stated in Fath al-Qadir, from the chapter of adhan, that greeting one who is defecating is haram, and it is not hidden what is in it, and Allah knows best. He said in al-Nahr: And additional places were added, and the best thing is what Shaykh Sadr al-Din al-Ghazzi collected, who said: Your greeting is disliked to those you will hear, and after it appears, it is sunnah and prescribed. Repeated fiqh, sitting for judgment, and those who research in knowledge, leave them to benefit. And chess players and the like, and one who is with his family enjoying, eating except if you are hungry, and from it you learn that it does not prevent the prayer, the reciter, the dhakir, the speaker, the preacher, and those who listen to them and hear, the mu'adhdhin also, the muqim, the teacher, likewise young women, women are prevented. And leave the disbeliever, the one with exposed 'awrah, and the one in the state of defecation is uglier. And I added to it the student with his teacher as in al-Qunyah and al-Mughni and the pigeon flyer, and I attached it and said: Leave.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is an extended intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether greeting a worshipper (salat) and responding by gesture invalidates the prayer. The commentator begins by noting that the authentic position (zahir al-riwayah) of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad is that it does not invalidate (laysa bi mufsid). He then introduces a critic who misunderstood the negation 'and he should not respond by gesture' as implying that if one does respond, it invalidates. The commentator refutes this, explaining that the negation simply prohibits initiation of greeting, not that responding invalidates. He cites the hadith of Suhayb and Ibn 'Umar showing the Prophet responded by gesture during prayer, which establishes permissibility. Some scholars like al-Zayla'i attempt to explain away these hadith, but the commentator prefers the straightforward interpretation. Then the discussion turns to shaking hands (musafaha) during prayer. Al-Walwaliji held it invalidates because it is a greeting, while others say it is 'meaningful speech' (kalam ma'na). The commentator favors the view of al-Nahr that shaking hands is invalidating because it is a lot of action ('amal kathir), unlike a simple gesture. Then the passage lists various persons to whom greeting is disliked, including the one praying, reading, sitting for judgment, etc. The poem by Sadr al-Din al-Ghazzi summarizes these situations. The overall conclusion is that responding by gesture does not invalidate prayer, but shaking hands might be considered invalidating due to excessive action. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that responding by gesture is permissible and not invalidating, and the dislike (karahah) for greeting the worshipper is tanzihi (slight dislike), not tahrimi.

Key Terms
الرد بالإشارة (al-radd bil-ishara): Responding to a greeting by a hand gesture or nod during prayer, without speaking.
المصافحة (al-musafaha): Shaking hands, which during prayer is considered a lot of action and may invalidate according to many scholars.
كلام معنى (kalam ma'na): Meaningful communication without actual speech, such as gestures, signs, or nods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what invalidates prayer when responding to a greeting?
A) Any response, including gesture
B) Only verbal response
C) Only shaking hands
D) Both verbal response and excessive movement such as shaking hands

Key Takeaway
Responding to a greeting by gesture during prayer is permissible and does not invalidate, but shaking hands may invalidate if it involves a lot of action.

Transferring from One Prayer to Another During Salat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of the second prayer when order is breached.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sahib tartib starts a different prayer after one rak'ah of Zuhr and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf from Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Starting another prayer after one rak'ah of Zuhr invalidates Zuhr; for a sahib tartib, the second prayer becomes voluntary.

Have you ever wondered what happens if you switch prayers mid-salat? This lesson tackles a precise scenario: a person who is required to pray in order (sahib tartib) prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then begins Asr or a voluntary prayer. The Hanafi school offers a nuanced ruling based on a key principle: invalidation of the description does not invalidate the essence. We'll explore the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Muhammad al-Shaybani, and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Actor
Determine the precise facts: the person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr, then starts Asr or a voluntary prayer. Is he a sahib tartib (obliged to maintain order) or not? The passage focuses on the case where he is a sahib tartib.
Sahib tartib condition is crucial: order is required for fard prayers unless excused by narrow time or many missed prayers.
2
Understand the Invalidation of the First Prayer
The Zuhr prayer is invalidated because starting another prayer contradicts the first. The person cannot have two intentions simultaneously, so he exits the first prayer by valid entry into the second.
This is agreed upon: the first prayer is batil (invalid).
3
Analyze the Disagreement on the Second Prayer
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the second prayer becomes voluntary (nafl), while Muhammad al-Shaybani may hold it remains fard. Understand the basis of each view.
The passage only mentions Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, implying disagreement.
4
Apply the Principle 'Butlan al-Wasf...'
The key principle: invalidation of the description (fardiyya) does not necessitate invalidation of the essence (the prayer itself). Thus, the Asr prayer loses its description of being fard due to the breach of order, but the prayer itself remains valid as voluntary.
This principle is used by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf to justify the second prayer becoming nafl.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: if the second prayer becomes voluntary, the person has performed a nafl and must later repeat the fard Zuhr. If it remained fard, he would have performed Asr and must make up Zuhr. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
Understanding this difference helps in giving correct fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وافتتاح العصر أو التطوع لا الظهر بعد ركعة الظهر) أي يفسدها انتقاله صلاة إلى أخرى مغايرة للأولى، فقوله بعد ركعة الظهر ظرف للافتتاح وصورتها: صلى ركعة من الظهر ثم افتتح العصر أو التطوع بتكبيره فقد أفسد الظهر. وتفسير المسألة أن لا يكون صاحب ترتيب بأن بطل عنه بضيق الوقت أو بكثرة الفوائت فإن كان صاحب ترتيب فالمنتقل إلى العصر متطوع عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأنه لا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل عندهما، وإن انتقل إلى عصر سابق على الظهر فقد انتقض وصف الفرضية قبل الدخول في العصر للترتيب فإنما انتقل عن تطوع لا فرض كذا في الكافي. وإنما بطل ظهره لأنه صح شروعه في غيره لأنه نوى تحصيل ما ليس بحاصل فيخرج عنه ضرورة المنافاة بينهما، فمناط الخروج عن الأولى صحة الشروع في المغاير ولو من وجه، فلذا لو كان منفرداً
His statement: (And starting Asr or voluntary prayer, not Zuhr after a rak'ah of Zuhr) i.e., that his transfer from one prayer to another different from the first invalidates it. So his statement 'after a rak'ah of Zuhr' is a time phrase for the start, and its example: He prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr then started Asr or voluntary prayer with takbir, and thus he has invalidated Zuhr. The explanation of the issue is that he is not a sahib tartib (one with order), because order is lifted from him due to narrow time or many missed prayers. If he is a sahib tartib, then the one who transfers to Asr is a volunteer according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because from the invalidation of the description (of fardiyya) does not necessitate the invalidation of the essence according to them. And if he transferred to an Asr that is earlier than Zuhr, then the description of fardiyya is voided before entering into Asr due to order, so he only transferred from a voluntary act, not a fard. Thus in al-Kafi. And the invalidation of his Zuhr is because his starting something else is valid, because he intended to attain what is not attained, so he exits out of necessity of contradiction between them. So the criterion for exit from the first is the validity of starting in the different, even in one aspect. So if he was alone...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation regarding the invalidation of prayer when one transfers from one prayer to another. The commentator explains the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'And starting Asr or voluntary prayer, not Zuhr after a rak'ah of Zuhr.' That is, if a person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then starts Asr (or a voluntary prayer) with the opening takbir, he has invalidated his Zuhr prayer. The condition is that he is not a 'sahib tartib' (one who is required to pray in order), because the order is waived for him either due to time being too narrow (e.g., fear of missing Asr) or due to having many missed prayers (fawa'it). If he is a sahib tartib (i.e., he is required to pray Zuhr before Asr), then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, when he starts Asr before completing Zuhr, he becomes a volunteer (mutatawwi') in that Asr prayer. Why? Because the description of fardiyya (obligatory nature) of Asr is invalidated due to the breach of order, but the essence (asl) of the prayer remains as a voluntary act. So he has effectively left the Zuhr prayer and entered a voluntary prayer. Thus his Zuhr is invalidated. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani might differ? The text only mentions Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The ruling is based on the principle that starting a different prayer, even if it becomes voluntary, contradicts the first prayer, so the first is invalidated. The exit from the first prayer is caused by the valid entry into a different prayer, even if only in one aspect (like intention).

Key Terms
صاحب ترتيب (sahib tartib): A person who is required to pray the five daily prayers in their prescribed order (Zuhr before Asr, etc.). The obligation of order is lifted only when there is a valid excuse like narrow time or many missed prayers.
الوصف (al-wasf): The description or attribute of a prayer, such as being fard (obligatory). The essence (asl) of the prayer is the act of praying itself, while the obligation is an attribute.
بطلان الوصف لا يلزم منه بطلان الأصل (butlan al-wasf la yalzam minhu butlan al-asl): A principle meaning that the invalidation of a description (like fardiyya) does not necessitate the invalidation of the essence (the prayer itself). Thus, a prayer can become voluntary while remaining a valid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a person who is a sahib tartib (must pray in order) prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then begins Asr, what is the status of the Asr prayer?
A) It is valid as fard Asr.
B) It becomes a voluntary (nafl) prayer.
C) It is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is permissible as fard but he must repeat Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
The principle that invalidation of the description does not invalidate the essence allows a prayer to become voluntary when order is breached, a unique Hanafi contribution.

Handshake During Prayer: Does It Invalidate?
Commentary on handshake and greeting during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether handshake invalidates prayer and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Handshake does not invalidate prayer, but it is disliked — a gesture is not speech.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a debate among Hanafi scholars about whether shaking hands during prayer invalidates it. Al-Walwaliji and al-Zayla'i argue it does, but the commentator refutes them by analogy with gestures, which are not invalidating. We will trace the proofs and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? Handshake during prayer. What is the disputed ruling? Does it invalidate?
The text presents two opposing views.
2
Examine the opposing proofs
Al-Walwaliji argues it is a greeting, which is invalidating. Al-Zayla'i argues it is meaningful talk, also invalidating.
These are based on the principle that external speech or meaningful talk invalidates prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator responds that replying with a hand gesture is also meaningful talk, yet hadiths indicate it does not invalidate. Therefore, by analogy, handshake should be similar.
The key analogy: gesture = meaningful talk, but not invalidating.
4
Identify the tarjih
The preferred view is that handshake does not invalidate, supported by al-Halabi and al-Bahr al-Raiq. The prayer remains valid but it is disliked (makruh).
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: one should avoid handshake during prayer, but if it occurs, the prayer is still valid.
This avoids unnecessary invalidation.
