الولوالجي لفسادها بالمصافحة بأنها سلام وهو مفسد . وعلل الزيعلي بأنها كلام معنى ويرد عليه أن الرد بالإشارة كلام معنى، فالظاهر استواء حكمهما وهو عدم الفساد للأحاديث الواردة في ذلك . ثم اعلم أنه يكره السلام على المصلي والقارىء والجالس للقضاء أو البحث في الفقه أو التخلي، ولو سلم عليهم لا يجب عليهم الرد لأنه في غير محله . كذا ذكر الشارح . وصرح في فتح القدير من باب الأذان أن السلام على المتغوظ حرام ولا يخفى ما فيه إذ الدليل ليس بقطعي والله سبحانه أعلم .
من
قوله : ( وافتتاح العصر أو التطوع لا الظهر بعد ركعة الظهر) أي يفسدها انتقاله صلاة إلى أخرى مغايرة للأولى، فقوله بعد ركعة الظهر ظرف للافتتاح وصورتها: صلى ركعة من الظهر ثم افتتح العصر أو التطوع بتكبيره فقد أفسد الظهر. وتفسير المسألة أن لا يكون صاحب ترتيب بأن بطل عنه بضيق الوقت أو بكثرة الفوائت فإن كان صاحب ترتيب فالمنتقل إلى العصر متطوع عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لأنه لا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل عندهما، وإن انتقل إلى عصر سابق على الظهر فقد انتقض وصف الفرضية قبل الدخول في العصر للترتيب فإنما انتقل عن تطوع لا .فرض كذا في الكافي. وإنما بطل ظهره لأنه صح شروعه في غيره لأنه نوى تحصيل ما ليس بحاصل فيخرج عنه ضرورة المنافاة بينهما، فمناط الخروج عن الأولى صحة الشروع في المغاير ولو من وجه، فلذا لو كان منفرداً
يوهم
خلاف
الرد فيه بمعنى جواب التحية بقرينة المقام والاستعمال، ولو كان بمعنى عدم القبول والنهي عن السلام كان الواجب أن يقال فلم يجب سلامي أو لم يقبل أو نهاني ونحو ذلك مما لا المراد، وحمل الأدلة على المتبادر منها أولى وغيره تعسف لا يصار إليه إلا بملجيء قوله : (ويرد عليه أن الرد بالإشارة كلام معنى قال في النهر : فالأولى أن يعلل الفساد بالمصافحة بأنه عمل كثير بخلاف الرد باليد ا هـ. وهو ظاهر كلام الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرح المنية قوله : (ثم اعلم أنه يكره السلام
الخ) قال في النهر : وزيد عليه مواضع وأحسن من جمعها الشيخ صدر الدين الغزي فقال : سلامك مكروه على من ستسمع ومن بعد ما أبدى يسن ويشرع مکرر فقه جالس لقضائه ومن بحثوا في العلم دعهم لينفعوا ولعاب شطرنج وشبه بخلقهم ومن هو مع أهل له يتمتع أكلا إلا إذا كنت جائعاً وتعلم منه أنه ليس يـمـنــع مصل وتال ذاكر ومحدث خطيب ومن يصغي إليهم ويسمع مؤذن أيضاً أو مــقــيــم مــدرس كذا الأجنبيات الفتيات تمنع ودع كافراً ومـكـشـوف عورة ومن هو في حال التغوط أشنع وقد زدت عليه المتفقه على أستاذه كما في القنية والمغني ومطير الحمام وألحقته فقلت :
ودع
كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها ۱۷
في فرض فكبر ينوي الاقتداء أو النفل أو الواجب أو شرع في جنازة فجيء بأخرى فكبر ينويهما أو الثانية يصير مستأنفاً على الثانية فقط بخلاف ما إذا لم ينو شيئاً، ولو كان مقتدياً فكبر للانفراد يفسد ما أدى قبله ويصير مفتتحاً ما أداه ثانياً . وقوله لا الظهر» يعني لو صلى ركعة من الظهر فكبر ينوي الاستئناف للظهر بعينها فلا يفسد ما أداه فيحتسب بتلك الركعة حتى لو لم يقعد فيما بقي القعدة الأخيرة باعتبارها فسدت الصلاة فلغت النية الثانية، وتفرع عليه ما ذكره الولوالجي إذا صلى الظهر أربعاً فلما سلم تذكر أنه ترك سجدة منها ساهياً ثم قام واستقبل الصلاة وصلى أربعاً وسلم وذهب فسد ظهره لأن نية دخوله في الظهر ثانياً وقع لغواً، فإذا صلى ركعة فقد خلط المكتوبة بالنافلة قبل الفراغ من المكتوبة .اهـ. ومعلوم أن هذا إذا لم يتلفظ بلسانه، فإن قال نويت أن أصلي إلى آخره فسدت الأولى وصار مستأنفاً للمنوي ثانياً مطلقاً لأن الكلام مفسد. وقيد بالصلاة لأنه لو صام قضاء رمضان وأمسك بعد الفجر ثم نوى بعده نفلاً لم يخرج عنه بنية النفل لأن الفرض والنفل في الصلاة جنسان مختلفان لا رجحان لأحدهما على الآخر في التحريمة وهما في الصوم والزكاة جنس واحد. كذا في المحيط .
Al-Walwaliji said that invalidating it with a handshake is because it is a greeting and it invalidates. Al-Zayla'i reasoned that it is meaningful talk, and it is responded to that replying with a gesture is meaningful talk, so apparently both are equal and not invalidating due to the hadiths narrated about that. Then know that it is disliked to greet the one praying, reading, sitting for judgment, studying fiqh, or relieving oneself, and if one greets them, they are not obligated to reply because it is out of place. This is what the commentator mentioned. And in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter of adhan, it is stated that greeting one who is defecating is haram, but it is not hidden what is in it since the evidence is not decisive, and Allah knows best. From his saying: (And opening the 'Asr or supererogatory, not Zuhr after a rak'ah of Zuhr) meaning, his transferring from one prayer to another different from the first invalidates it. So his saying 'after a rak'ah of Zuhr' is an adverbial for the opening, and its form is: he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr then opened 'Asr or supererogatory with takbir, so he invalidated Zuhr. And the interpretation of the issue is that he is not a person of order, because the order is lost due to time constraint or many missed prayers. If he is a person of order, then the one transferring to 'Asr is a supererogatory worshipper according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, because the invalidation of the description does not necessitate the invalidation of the essence according to them. And if he transferred to an 'Asr that is before Zuhr, then the description of obligatory status is nullified before entering into 'Asr due to order, so he transferred from supererogatory, not obligation. So in al-Kafi. And his Zuhr is invalidated because his starting in another prayer is valid because he intended to obtain what is not obtained, so he exits due to the necessity of contradiction between them. So the criterion for exiting the first is the validity of starting the different one, even if in some aspect. So if he was alone, it suggests a difference. The reply here means the answer to the greeting by context and usage, and if it meant non-acceptance or prohibition of greeting, it would be necessary to say 'he did not accept my greeting' or 'he prohibited' etc., which is not intended. And carrying the evidence on the obvious meaning is better, and otherwise is forced and cannot be resorted to except with necessity. His saying: (And it is responded that replying with a gesture is meaningful talk. Al-Nahr said: The better is to explain the invalidity of handshake as being much action, unlike the reply with the hand. This is apparent from the words of Sheikh Ibrahim al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munya. His saying: (Then know that it is disliked to greet...) Al-Nahr said: Additional places were mentioned, and the best summarizer is Sheikh Sadr al-Din al-Ghazzi who said: Your greeting is disliked to those you will hear... etc. (the poem). Then: In a fard he said takbir intending iqtida' or nafl or wajib, or started on a janazah then another came and he said takbir intending both or the second, he becomes starting anew on the second only, unlike if he did not intend anything. And if he was a follower and said takbir for munfarid, it invalidates what he performed and he becomes starting what he performed second. And his saying 'not Zuhr' means if he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr and said takbir intending to renew Zuhr itself, he does not invalidate what he performed, so that rak'ah counts. This is if he did not speak. If he said 'I intend to pray...' then the first is invalidated and he becomes starting what he intended second absolutely because speech invalidates. And it is restricted to prayer because if he fasted qada' of Ramadan and stopped after dawn then intended nafl later, he does not exit from it by intending nafl, because the obligatory and nafl in prayer are two different types with no superiority of one over the other in the opening takbir, while in fasting and zakat they are one type. This is in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the chapter of what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. It opens with a dispute between two Hanafi scholars: al-Walwaliji holds that shaking hands invalidates prayer because it is a greeting (salam) which is an invalidating act, while al-Zayla'i argues it is meaningful talk (kalam ma'na), which also invalidates. The commentator refutes both by noting that replying with a hand gesture is meaningful talk, yet it is not invalidating according to hadith. Thus the apparent ruling is that handshake does not invalidate. Next, the text discusses the dislike of greeting people in certain states: praying, reading, judging, studying fiqh, or relieving oneself. If greeted, they are not obligated to respond. A note from Fath al-Qadir declares greeting one who is defecating as haram, but the commentator questions the certainty of the evidence. The commentary then turns to the phrase 'opening 'Asr or supererogatory, not Zuhr after a rak'ah of Zuhr' from the matn. If a person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then opens 'Asr or a supererogatory prayer with takbir, he invalidates his Zuhr. This applies when he is not a 'person of order' (sahib tartib), i.e., when the order of prayers is lost due to time constraints or many missed prayers. If he is a person of order and transfers to an 'Asr that is due after Zuhr, he becomes a supererogatory worshipper according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the invalidity of the description (obligatoriness) does not invalidate the essence of the prayer. If he transfers to an 'Asr that is due before Zuhr, he violates the order and becomes a supererogatory worshipper, so his Zuhr is invalidated. The passage then digresses into a discussion on the meaning of 'reply' (رد) in the context of greeting, clarifying that it means answering the greeting, not rejecting it. It cites al-Nahr preferring to explain handshake as much action rather than speech. A poem by Sadr al-Din al-Ghazzi lists those to whom greeting is disliked, including a person praying, reading, speaking, listening, a mu'adhdhin, a teacher, etc. The commentary returns to the matn 'not Zuhr' with more scenarios: if a follower intends to leave the imam or start a new prayer, the ruling depends on intention. For example, if he is praying a fard and says takbir intending to become a follower or to switch to nafl or wajib, or if multiple janazah prayers are present, his action is evaluated. The text also discusses the case of one who prays Zuhr then remembers missing a sajdah and starts Zuhr again: it invalidates the first because the second intention is void. The commentary concludes by distinguishing between prayer and fasting: in prayer, obligatory and supererogatory are different types and cannot be mixed, while in fasting they are the same type.

Key Terms
صاحب ترتيب (sāhib tartīb): A person who must maintain the order of prayers due to not having many missed prayers or time constraints.
كلام معنى (kalām ma‘nā): Meaningful talk that communicates a message but not necessarily words; includes gestures.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir of prayer, which distinguishes the type (fard/nafl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi ruling on handshake during prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It does not invalidate but is disliked.
C) It is permissible without dislike.
D) It invalidates only if accompanied by speech.

Key Takeaway
Handshake during prayer does not invalidate, but it is disliked and should be avoided.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Transferring Prayer Intention: When Does It Invalidate?
Commentary on transfer of prayer intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that starting a different prayer after one rak'ah of the first invalidates the first, and distinguish the case of a sahib tartib.

Core Idea
Intending a different prayer after one rak'ah invalidates the first because prayer types are distinct.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the scenario where a person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then intends to start 'Asr or a supererogatory prayer. The ruling is that it invalidates Zuhr, unless the person is a sahib tartib. The lesson unpacks the conditions and the Hanafi ikhtilaf on intention changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr then opens 'Asr or nafl with takbir.
The first prayer (Zuhr) is incomplete.
2
Determine if the person is sahib tartib
Sahib tartib means the order of prayers is still binding due to few missed prayers and no time constraint.
If not sahib tartib, the order is waived.
3
Apply the ruling for non-sahib tartib
If not sahib tartib, the Zuhr is invalidated because the new intention is valid.
The intention to start a different prayer is a valid exit from the first.
4
Note the ikhtilaf for sahib tartib
If sahib tartib transfers to an 'Asr that is due after Zuhr, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the intention to 'Asr is valid but it becomes nafl because the Zuhr is still obligatory.
This is because invalidation of description does not invalidate essence.
5
Distinguish between transfer to earlier or later prayer
If transferring to an 'Asr due before Zuhr, the order is violated, so the Zuhr becomes nafl and the transfer invalidates it.
The order requirement causes the description of fardiyya to be lost.

الولوالجي لفسادها بالمصافحة بأنها سلام وهو مفسد . وعلل الزيعلي بأنها كلام معنى ويرد عليه أن الرد بالإشارة كلام معنى، فالظاهر استواء حكمهما وهو عدم الفساد للأحاديث الواردة في ذلك . ثم اعلم أنه يكره السلام على المصلي والقارىء والجالس للقضاء أو البحث في الفقه أو التخلي، ولو سلم عليهم لا يجب عليهم الرد لأنه في غير محله . كذا ذكر الشارح . وصرح في فتح القدير من باب الأذان أن السلام على المتغوظ حرام ولا يخفى ما فيه إذ الدليل ليس بقطعي والله سبحانه أعلم .

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the chapter of what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. It opens with a dispute between two Hanafi scholars: al-Walwaliji holds that shaking hands invalidates prayer because it is a greeting (salam) which is an invalidating act, while al-Zayla'i argues it is meaningful talk (kalam ma'na), which also invalidates. The commentator refutes both by noting that replying with a hand gesture is meaningful talk, yet it is not invalidating according to hadith. Thus the apparent ruling is that handshake does not invalidate. Next, the text discusses the dislike of greeting people in certain states: praying, reading, judging, studying fiqh, or relieving oneself. If greeted, they are not obligated to respond. A note from Fath al-Qadir declares greeting one who is defecating as haram, but the commentator questions the certainty of the evidence. The commentary then turns to the phrase 'opening 'Asr or supererogatory, not Zuhr after a rak'ah of Zuhr' from the matn. If a person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then opens 'Asr or a supererogatory prayer with takbir, he invalidates his Zuhr. This applies when he is not a 'person of order' (sahib tartib), i.e., when the order of prayers is lost due to time constraints or many missed prayers. If he is a person of order and transfers to an 'Asr that is due after Zuhr, he becomes a supererogatory worshipper according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the invalidity of the description (obligatoriness) does not invalidate the essence of the prayer. If he transfers to an 'Asr that is due before Zuhr, he violates the order and becomes a supererogatory worshipper, so his Zuhr is invalidated. The passage then digresses into a discussion on the meaning of 'reply' (رد) in the context of greeting, clarifying that it means answering the greeting, not rejecting it. It cites al-Nahr preferring to explain handshake as much action rather than speech. A poem by Sadr al-Din al-Ghazzi lists those to whom greeting is disliked, including a person praying, reading, speaking, listening, a mu'adhdhin, a teacher, etc. The commentary returns to the matn 'not Zuhr' with more scenarios: if a follower intends to leave the imam or start a new prayer, the ruling depends on intention. For example, if he is praying a fard and says takbir intending to become a follower or to switch to nafl or wajib, or if multiple janazah prayers are present, his action is evaluated. The text also discusses the case of one who prays Zuhr then remembers missing a sajdah and starts Zuhr again: it invalidates the first because the second intention is void. The commentary concludes by distinguishing between prayer and fasting: in prayer, obligatory and supererogatory are different types and cannot be mixed, while in fasting they are the same type.

Key Terms
صاحب ترتيب (sāhib tartīb): A person who must maintain the order of prayers due to not having many missed prayers or time constraints.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir of prayer, which distinguishes the type (fard/nafl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person who is not a sahib tartib prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and then intends 'Asr, what happens to the Zuhr?
A) It becomes nafl and continues.
B) It is invalidated.
C) It remains valid as Zuhr.
D) It is suspended.

Key Takeaway
Intending a different prayer after one rak'ah invalidates the first unless the person is a sahib tartib, in which case the new intention becomes nafl.

Reading from the Mushaf During Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Ruling on reading from a physical copy of the Quran during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reading from a mushaf in prayer, explain the two companions' opposing view, and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Core Idea
Reading from a mushaf invalidates prayer per Abu Hanifa; the two companions deem it valid but disliked.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer when the worshipper reads directly from a physical copy of the Quran. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is invalidated, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider the prayer valid but makruh (disliked). The discussion revolves around whether handling the mushaf constitutes excessive action (amal kathir) or whether reading from it is akin to receiving dictation from another person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine the specific act under dispute: reading from a physical mushaf during prayer.
The act is not recitation from memory, but reading the written text.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa rules that the prayer is invalid (fasid). He gives two reasons: (1) handling the mushaf is excessive action, and (2) reading from it is like receiving dictation from another person.
These are two independent arguments; the second is preferred by later scholars.
3
State the position of the two companions
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say the prayer is valid (tammah) but disliked (makruh) because it resembles the practice of the People of the Book.
They view it as an act of worship annexed to another worship.
4
Analyze the evidence for Abu Hanifa's view
Besides the two reasons, a hadith from Ibn Abbas is cited: 'Umar forbade leading prayer while holding a mushaf.' The principle that a prohibition in prayer implies invalidity supports Abu Hanifa.
This hadith is used as additional evidence, though its chain may be weak.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Al-Kafi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi validate Abu Hanifa's second reason, and the relied-upon position is that reading from a mushaf invalidates the prayer.
Some later Hanafi scholars follow the companions for ease, but the majority hold the stricter view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وقراءته من مصحف) أي يفسدها عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : هي تامة لأنها عبادة انضافت إلى عبادة إلا أنه يكره لأنه تشبه بصنيع أهل الكتاب ولأبي حنيفة وجهان: أحدهما أن حمل المصحف والنظر فيه وتقليب الأوراق عمل كثير . الثاني أنه تلقن من المصحف فصار كما إذا تلقن من غيره. وعلى هذا الثاني لا فرق بين الموضوع والمحمول عنده، وعلى الأول المصنف يفترقان. وصحح في الكافي الثاني وقال : إنها تفسد بكل حال تبعاً لما صححه شمس الأئمة السرخسي. وربما يستدل لأبي حنيفة كما ذكره العلامة الحلبي بما أخرجه ابن أبي داود عن ابن عباس قال : نهانا أمير المؤمنين أن نؤم الناس في المصحف فإن الأصل كون النهي يقتضي الفساد وأراد بالمصحف المكتوب فيه شيء من القرآن فإن الصحيح أنه لو قرأ من اه.
His saying: (And his reading from a mushaf) i.e., it invalidates according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions said it is complete because one worship annexed to another worship, except that it is disliked because it resembles the practice of the People of the Book. Abu Hanifa has two aspects: one is that carrying the mushaf, looking into it, and turning pages is much action; the second is that he receives dictation from the mushaf, so it becomes like receiving dictation from someone else. According to this second aspect, there is no difference between a held and placed mushaf according to him, while according to the first, they differ. Al-Kafi validated the second and said it invalidates in any case, following the correction of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. And perhaps evidence for Abu Hanifa is cited by al-Halabi from what Ibn Abi Dawud narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The Commander of the Faithful forbade us from leading people in prayer with a mushaf' and the principle is that a prohibition necessitates invalidity. By mushaf he means what contains something of the Quran, for the correct is that if he reads from it...
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of reading from a mushaf (written copy of the Quran) during prayer. There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa holds that it invalidates the prayer, while the companions say the prayer is valid but disliked. The companions reason that it is an act of worship added to another worship, but it is disliked due to resembling the People of the Book. Abu Hanifa gives two reasons: first, handling the mushaf, looking, and turning pages constitutes excessive action (amal kathir), which invalidates prayer; second, the reciter is effectively receiving dictation from the mushaf, making it as if he is being prompted by another person, which breaks the directness of recitation. According to the second reason, there is no difference whether the mushaf is held or placed, but according to the first, a held mushaf involves more action. Al-Kafi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi validate the second reason, holding that reading from a mushaf invalidates in all cases. Evidence is cited from a hadith of Ibn Abbas that 'Umar forbade leading prayer while holding a mushaf, and the principle that a prohibition in such contexts implies invalidity. The correct view in the Hanafi school is that reading from a mushaf invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
مصحف (muṣḥaf): A physical copy of the Quran, whether held or placed.
عمل كثير (‘amal kathīr): Excessive movement or action that negates the required stillness in prayer.
تلقن (talaqqun): Receiving dictation or prompting from another, which breaks the direct recitation of the worshipper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of reading from a mushaf during prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) It is valid but disliked.
B) It invalidates the prayer.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is prohibited but does not invalidate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative ruling is that reading from a physical mushaf invalidates the prayer, based on the authority of Abu Hanifa's reasoning adopted by later scholars.

Changing Intention During Prayer: The Second Takbir
Explains the effect of a second takbir on intention during fard prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person in fard prayer says a second takbir with a new intention and distinguish the effect of speaking the intention.

Core Idea
A new takbir with a changed intention starts a new prayer; speaking the intention invalidates the first prayer entirely.

The Hanafi school treats the opening takbir (tahrimah) as the boundary of prayer. Changing intention without a new takbir does not affect the current prayer, but a second takbir with a new intention abandons the first and begins a new one. Speaking the intention, however, nullifies the prayer itself due to speech being an invalidator. This lesson unpacks these nuanced scenarios from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Context
The person is in a fard prayer and says a second takbir with a new intention (e.g., to follow an imam, to pray nafl, wajib, or another funeral prayer). Determine the initial prayer type and the new intention.
The second takbir is a deliberate action that may interrupt the first prayer.
2
Determine the Effect on the First Prayer
According to the text, if the new intention is different from the original prayer (e.g., fard to nafl), the first prayer is abandoned and the person becomes 'starting anew on the second only'. However, if he does not intend anything specific, the first prayer remains unaffected.
This is distinct from merely intending in the heart; a new takbir is required.
3
Note the Exception: Intending the Same Prayer
If he intended to restart the same prayer (e.g., another zuhr after one rak'ah), the first rak'ah counts and the second intention is void. But if he later neglects the final sitting, the entire prayer becomes invalid.
This shows that the second takbir does not automatically nullify; it depends on the intention.
4
Apply the Distinction Between Takbir and Speech
All the above rulings apply only if the intention is made silently by takbir. If he utters the intention aloud (e.g., 'I intend to pray...'), that speech itself invalidates the first prayer absolutely, and he starts the newly intended prayer immediately.
Speech is a major invalidator (mufsid) in prayer, unlike mere intention by takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في فرض فكبر ينوي الاقتداء أو النفل أو الواجب أو شرع في جنازة فجيء بأخرى فكبر ينويهما أو الثانية يصير مستأنفاً على الثانية فقط بخلاف ما إذا لم ينو شيئاً، ولو كان مقتدياً فكبر للانفراد يفسد ما أدى قبله ويصير مفتتحاً ما أداه ثانياً . وقوله لا الظهر» يعني لو صلى ركعة من الظهر فكبر ينوي الاستئناف للظهر بعينها فلا يفسد ما أداه فيحتسب بتلك الركعة حتى لو لم يقعد فيما بقي القعدة الأخيرة باعتبارها فسدت الصلاة فلغت النية الثانية، وتفرع عليه ما ذكره الولوالجي إذا صلى الظهر أربعاً فلما سلم تذكر أنه ترك سجدة منها ساهياً ثم قام واستقبل الصلاة وصلى أربعاً وسلم وذهب فسد ظهره لأن نية دخوله في الظهر ثانياً وقع لغواً، فإذا صلى ركعة فقد خلط المكتوبة بالنافلة قبل الفراغ من المكتوبة .اهـ. ومعلوم أن هذا إذا لم يتلفظ بلسانه، فإن قال نويت أن أصلي إلى آخره فسدت الأولى وصار مستأنفاً للمنوي ثانياً مطلقاً لأن الكلام مفسد. وقيد بالصلاة لأنه لو صام قضاء رمضان وأمسك بعد الفجر ثم نوى بعده نفلاً لم يخرج عنه بنية النفل لأن الفرض والنفل في الصلاة جنسان مختلفان لا رجحان لأحدهما على الآخر في التحريمة وهما في الصوم والزكاة جنس واحد. كذا في المحيط .
قوله: (فقد انتقض وصف الفرضية قبل الدخول في العصر) هذا إنما يظهر على قول أبي يوسف، أما على قول أبي حنيفة ،فلا لأن فساده موقوف على قضاء العصر قبل صيرورتها ستاً تأمل قوله : (يصير مستأنفاً على الثانية فقط) أي على الصلاة الثانية أي ما نواه ثانيا في الصور الأربع لا في الأخيرة فقط كما توهمه بعضهم فاعترض بأن ما ذكره مسلم فيما إذا كبر ينوي الثانية، أما إذا نواهما يصير مستأنفاً عليهما فتدبر . ثم ما ذكره المؤلف هنا مأخوذ من الفتح ونقله عنه في النهر وفي النهاية ما يخالفه حيث قال وفي نوادر الصلاة لو صلى الرجل على جنازة فكبر تكبيرة ثم جيء بأخرى فوضعت بجنبها فإن كبر التكبيرة الثانية ينوي الصلاة على الأولى أو عليهما أو لا نية له فهو على الجنازة الأولى على حاله يتمها ثم يستقبل الصلاة على الثانية لأنه نوى اتحاد الموجود وهو لغو، وإن كبر ينوي الصلاة على الثانية يصير رافضاً للأولى شارعاً في الثانية لأنه نوى
In a fard prayer, if he says the takbir intending to follow [an imam], or nafl, or wajib, or he began a funeral prayer and another was brought and he says the takbir intending both or the second, he becomes starting anew on the second only, contrary to if he did not intend anything. If he was following [an imam] and says the takbir to pray alone, it invalidates what he performed before and he becomes starting what he performs second. And his statement: 'not the zuhr' means: if he prayed one rak'ah of zuhr and said the takbir intending to restart the same zuhr, it does not invalidate what he performed, so that rak'ah counts; even if he did not sit for the final sitting that remained, the prayer is invalid so the second intention becomes void. Branched from that is what al-Walwaliji mentioned: if he prayed zuhr four rak'ahs and upon taslim remembered that he accidentally left a sajdah, then stood and started prayer again and prayed four and made taslim and left, his zuhr is invalid because his intention to enter the zuhr a second time was void; if he prayed one rak'ah, he mixed fard with nafl before completing the fard. It is known that this is if he did not utter with his tongue; if he said 'I intend to pray...' etc., the first becomes invalid and he becomes starting the second intended absolutely, because speech invalidates. And it is restricted to prayer because if he fasted to make up Ramadan and refrained after dawn, then intended nafl after that, he does not exit from it by the nafl intention because fard and nafl in prayer are two different types with no preference of one over the other in the opening takbir, while in fasting and zakat they are one type. Thus in al-Muhit.
His statement: 'The description of fardiyah is nullified before entering 'asr' – this is apparent only according to Abu Yusuf; as for Abu Hanifa, no, because its invalidity is dependent on making up 'asr before it becomes six. Deliberate. His statement: 'He becomes starting anew on the second only' – i.e., the second prayer, meaning what he intended second in the four cases, not only the last as some imagined; they objected that what Muslim mentioned is when he says takbir intending the second; if he intends both, he becomes starting anew on both. So ponder. Then what the author mentioned here is taken from al-Fath and he transmitted it from it in al-Nahr, and in al-Nihayah there is something contradicting it: 'In Nawadir al-Salah: if a man prayed over a funeral and said one takbir, then another was brought and placed beside it, and he said the second takbir intending the prayer over the first, or both, or without intention, he continues the first funeral to completion, then starts the second, because he intended unity of what exists and it is void. If he said the takbir intending the prayer over the second, he becomes abandoning the first and starting the second, because he intended.'
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings on changing intention during prayer. It is part of the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The passage initially discusses scenarios where a person in a fard prayer says a second takbir with a new intention (to follow an imam, to pray nafl, wajib, or another funeral prayer). The ruling is that doing so makes him start anew on the second prayer only, unless he intended both, in which case he starts on both? Actually the text says 'يصير مستأنفاً على الثانية فقط' – he becomes starting the second only. Then it discusses the case of a follower who says takbir to pray alone: this invalidates the previous part and he starts over with the new intention. Next, the phrase 'لا الظهر' is explained: if someone prays one rak'ah of zuhr and then says takbir intending to restart the same zuhr prayer, the first rak'ah counts; but if he neglects the final sitting later, the whole prayer becomes corrupt and the second intention becomes void. The text then mentions a branch by al-Walwaliji: if someone prays four rak'ahs of zuhr, after taslim remembers he missed a sajdah, then stands and prays another four and finishes, his original zuhr is invalid because the second intention was void; after one rak'ah, he mixed fard and nafl before completing the fard. Importantly, these rulings apply only if he did not speak; if he uttered any intention aloud (e.g., 'I intend to pray...'), that speech itself invalidates the original prayer and he automatically starts the newly intended prayer. The ruling is specific to prayer, because fard and nafl in prayer are considered different categories with no preference in the opening takbir, whereas in fasting and zakat they are considered the same category (so an intention to change does not exit the original). Later, the commentary clarifies a statement about nullification of 'fardiyah' before entering 'asr': this applies according to Abu Yusuf, but according to Abu Hanifa, the invalidity depends on making up 'asr before it becomes six rak'ahs? The commentary also explains that 'becoming starting anew on the second only' refers to the second prayer among four possible cases, and corrects a misunderstanding that it applies only to the last case. Additionally, the Nawadir al-Salah case of funeral prayers is cited: if someone starts a funeral prayer, then another corpse is brought, his second takbir with intention to continue the first or both keeps him on the first, then he starts the second; if he intends the second, he abandons the first and starts the second. This is based on the principle that intention of unity is void because the existing corpse is the focus.

Key Terms
الاستئناف (al-isti'naf): Starting the prayer anew, as opposed to continuing the previous one.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions.
الكلام (al-kalam): Speech; in prayer it is a major invalidator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It becomes the same type as the intended prayer.
B) It is invalidated and he starts the new prayer.
C) It remains valid and he must finish it later.
D) He is considered to have combined both prayers.

Key Takeaway
A second takbir with a different intention abandons the first prayer; speech invalidates it absolutely.

Recitation from a Mus'haf During Prayer: The Hanafi Dispute
Explains the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on praying while reciting from a Quran copy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting from a mus'haf during prayer, distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the exception for a hafiz.

Core Idea
Reciting from a mus'haf invalidates the prayer for a non-hafiz but not for a memoriser.

When leading prayer or praying alone, may one recite from a written copy of the Quran? The Hanafi school has a nuanced ikhtilaf between the eponymous founder and his two principal students. This lesson unpacks the competing proofs, the two alternative causes for invalidity, and the important exception for one who has memorised the Quran. Understanding this dispute trains you to weigh conflicting evidence within the same school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa: recitation from a mus'haf invalidates the prayer. Note the two possible causes he gave: (1) excessive action (carrying, looking, turning pages), and (2) talaqqun (learning from the mus'haf as from a teacher).
The second cause (talaqqun) is later preferred as the correct illa.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the prayer is valid but makruh due to resemblance to the People of the Book.
For them, the act is fundamentally an act of worship added to worship, so it cannot be invalid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn rely on the principle that adding worship to worship does not vitiate the original; the only drawback is tashabbuh (imitation), which is disliked but does not nullify.
They also implicitly rely on the general permissibility of reciting the Quran in any state.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's two-causes and the narrated prohibition from Ibn 'Abbas: 'Umar forbade leading prayer from a mus'haf. The principle 'nahy yufid al-fasad' (prohibition implies invalidity) is applied. Also, the second cause (talaqqun) is deemed stronger because it covers both placed and carried copies.
The narration is zanni in both thubut and dalala, but the Hanafi usul accepts it as sufficient for deriving wujub or fasad.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, using a mus'haf in prayer renders the prayer invalid (must be repeated); according to the Sahibayn, it is valid but disliked. The mufta bihi position adopts Abu Hanifa's view except for a hafiz, where the Sahibayn's view is accepted (valid but makruh).
Also, the intent behind tashabbuh matters: if one does not intend imitation, even the dislike may drop according to some authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وقراءته من مصحف) أي يفسدها عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : هي تامة لأنها عبادة انضافت إلى عبادة إلا أنه يكره لأنه تشبه بصنيع أهل الكتاب ولأبي حنيفة وجهان: أحدهما أن حمل المصحف والنظر فيه وتقليب الأوراق عمل كثير . الثاني أنه تلقن من المصحف فصار كما إذا تلقن من غيره. وعلى هذا الثاني لا فرق بين الموضوع والمحمول عنده، وعلى الأول المصنف يفترقان. وصحح في الكافي الثاني وقال : إنها تفسد بكل حال تبعاً لما صححه شمس الأئمة السرخسي. وربما يستدل لأبي حنيفة كما ذكره العلامة الحلبي بما أخرجه ابن أبي داود عن ابن عباس قال : نهانا أمير المؤمنين أن نؤم الناس في المصحف فإن الأصل كون النهي يقتضي الفساد وأراد بالمصحف المكتوب فيه شيء من القرآن فإن الصحيح أنه لو قرأ من محراب فسدت كما هو مقتضى الوجه الثاني كما صرحوا به وأطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير وما إذا لم يكن حافظاً أو حافظاً للقرآن وهو إطلاق الجامع الصغير، وذهب بعضهم إلى أنه إنما تفسد إذا قرأ آيه وبعضهم إذا قرأ الفاتحة. وقال الرازي قول أبي حنيفة محمول على من لم يحفظ القرآن ولا يمكنه أن يقرأ إلا من مصحف، فأما الحافظ فلا تفسد صلاته في قولهم جميعاً وتبعه على ذلك السرخسي في جامعة الصغير على ما في النهاية وأبو نصر الصفار على ما في الذخيرة معللاً بأن هذه القراءة مضافة إلى حفظه لا إلى تلقنه من المصحف، وجزم به في فتح القدير والنهاية والتبيين وهو أوجه كما لا يخفى. وفي الظهيرية : ثم لم يذكر في الكتاب أنه إذا لم يكن قادراً إلا على القراءة من المصحف فصلى بغير قراءة هل تجوز والأصح أنها لا تجوز ا.هـ. ويخالفه ما في النهاية نقلاً عن مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وكان الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل يقول في التعليل لأبي حنيفة أجمعنا على أن الرجل إذا كان يمكنه أن يقرأ المصحف ولا يمكنه أن يقرأ على ظهر قلبه أنه لو صلى بغير قراءة أنه يجزئه، ولو كانت المصحف جائزة لما أبيحت الصلاة بغير قراءة ولكن الظاهر أنهما لا يسلمان هذه قال بعض المشايخ ا.هـ. والظاهر أن ما في الظهيرية متفرع على أن علة الفساد حمله والعمل الكثير فإذا لم يحفظ شيئاً على ظهر قلبه يمكنه أن يقرأ من المصحف وهو موضوع فليس أمياً لتجوز صلاته بغير قراءة، وما ذكره الإمام الفضلي متفرع على الصحيح من أن علة الفساد تلقنه ولو كان موضوعاً فحينئذ لا قدرة له على القراءة فكان أمياً، وبهذا ظهر أن تصحيح الظهيرية مفرع على الضعيف. وأطلق في المصلي فشمل الإمام والمنفرد، فما في الهداية من تقييده بالإمام اتفاقي كما في غاية البيان. ثم اعلم أن التشبيه بأهل الكتاب لا يكره في كل شيء فإنا نأكل ونشرب كما يفعلون إنما الحرام هو التشبه فيما كان مذموماً وفيما يقصد به التشبيه كذا ذكره قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير فعلى هذا لو لم يقصد التشبه لا يكره عندهما .
His statement: 'and his recitation from a mus'haf' means: it invalidates [the prayer] according to Abu Hanifa, but the two said: it is valid because it is an act of worship added to worship, except that it is disliked because it resembles the practice of the People of the Book. According to Abu Hanifa, there are two aspects: one is that carrying the mus'haf, looking into it, and turning pages is much action. The second is that he learns from the mus'haf, so it is as if he learns from someone else. According to the second, there is no difference between placed and carried according to him; according to the first, they differ. Al-Kafi corrected the second and said: it invalidates in any case, following Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. Possibly evidence for Abu Hanifa is as mentioned by al-Allama al-Halabi from Ibn Abi Dawud's narration from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Commander of the Faithful forbade us from leading people in prayer from a mus'haf' – for the principle of prohibition implies corruption. He meant the mus'haf in which something of the Quran is written. For the correct view is that if he recites from a mihrab it invalidates as per the second aspect. He made it general, covering little and much, and whether he is a hafiz or not – that is the absolute of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Some went that it only invalidates if he recites a verse, some if he recites al-Fatiha. Al-Razi said: Abu Hanifa's statement is applied to one who has not memorized the Quran and can only read from a mus'haf; as for the hafiz, his prayer is not invalidated in all their views. Al-Sarakhsi followed that in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir as in al-Nihayah, and Abu Nasr al-Saffar as in al-Dhakhirah, reasoning that this recitation is attributed to his memory, not to his learning from the mus'haf. It was definitively stated in Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihayah, and al-Tabyin, and it is the soundest view. In al-Zahiriyyah: 'Then it was not mentioned in the book whether if he is only able to read from a mus'haf and prays without recitation, is it permissible? The correct view: it is not permissible.' It contradicts what is in al-Nihayah from the Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam, and Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said in the reasoning for Abu Hanifa: 'We all agree that if a man can read the mus'haf but cannot recite from memory, if he prays without recitation it is sufficient for him; had recitation from the mus'haf been permissible, prayer without recitation would not have been allowed, but apparently they do not accept this, as some scholars said.' The apparent meaning is that what is in al-Zahiriyyah is based on the cause of invalidity being carrying and much action, so if he does not remember anything by heart and can read from a placed mus'haf, he is not illiterate so his prayer without recitation is not valid. What al-Imam al-Fadli mentioned is based on the correct view that the cause of invalidity is learning (talaqqun) even if placed, so then he has no ability to recite, so he is illiterate. Thus it becomes clear that the correction of al-Zahiriyyah is based on the weaker view. He gave it generality to the worshipper, including imam and individual. What is in al-Hidayah restricting to imam is indecisive. Then know: imitation of the People of the Book is not disliked in everything; indeed we eat and drink as they do. What is forbidden is imitation in what is blameworthy and in that which intends imitation. Thus Qadikhan in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir. According to this, if one does not intend imitation, it is not disliked according to the two.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling of reciting from a mus'haf (written copy of the Quran) during prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, reciting from a mus'haf invalidates the prayer, because either (a) carrying and turning pages is excessive movement, or (b) the recitation is learned from the mus'haf as if from a teacher, which breaks the principle of direct recitation. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the prayer is valid but makruh (disliked) due to resemblance to the People of the Book. The text notes that al-Kafi and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi preferred the second view (invalid in all cases). Evidence is cited from a narration of Ibn 'Abbas that 'Umar forbade leading prayer from a mus'haf, and the general principle that a prohibition implies corruption. However, al-Razi and others differentiate: if the person is a hafiz (has memorized the Quran), then reciting from the mus'haf does not invalidate because the recitation is from memory, not from the mus'haf. This is supported by Sarakhsi, Abu Nasr al-Saffar, and authors of Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihayah, and al-Tabyin. There is further discussion about someone who cannot recite from memory: according to al-Zahiriyyah, if he can only read from a mus'haf, it is not permissible to pray without recitation, but others say it is sufficient if he has no memory. This leads to two possible causes for invalidity: (1) carrying and much action (weak view), and (2) learning from the mus'haf (correct view). The passage concludes with a note on tashabbuh (imitation): not all imitation of the People of the Book is prohibited; only that which is blameworthy or intended as imitation. Qadikhan states that if one does not intend imitation, it is not disliked according to the two companions.

Key Terms
المصحف (al-mus'haf): A written copy of the Quran, whether held or placed.
التلقن (al-talaqqun): Receiving recitation from an external source (mus'haf or another person).
التشبه بأهل الكتاب (al-tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitab): Imitating the practices of Jews and Christians; disliked in matters blameworthy or intended as imitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position regarding reciting from a mus'haf during prayer?
A) It always invalidates the prayer, regardless of memorisation.
B) It invalidates the prayer only if the mus'haf is carried and pages are turned.
C) It invalidates the prayer for a non-hafiz, but for a hafiz the prayer is valid (though disliked).
D) It is always valid but disliked, as per the Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on reciting from a mus'haf in prayer depends crucially on whether the person is a hafiz; if not, the prayer is invalid.

Salah — Prayer

Reading from the Mus-haf During Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reading from mus-haf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reading from the mus-haf during prayer and explain the intra-madhhab dispute based on the cause of invalidation.

Core Idea
The cause of invalidation determines the ruling: for a hafiz, reading from the mus-haf does not invalidate prayer.

The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement about reading from the mus-haf during salah. The apparent absolute ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir states that it invalidates prayer, but later scholars differentiated based on whether the person is a hafiz. This lesson examines the two causes of invalidation—excessive action (amal katheer) versus learning from the mus-haf (talaqqun)—and how they lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The passage begins by stating the absolute ruling that reading from the mus-haf invalidates prayer, then introduces differences: some say it only invalidates if a verse is read, others if al-Fatiha is read, and later scholars introduce the hafiz/non-hafiz distinction.
Note the shift from absolute to conditional rulings.
2
Trace the two causes of invalidation
Two causes are identified: (1) carrying the mus-haf and performing excessive action (amal katheer), and (2) learning/reciting from the mus-haf (talaqqun). Each leads to a different treatment of the hafiz.
The cause is central to the ruling (taliil).
3
Map each cause to the respective ruling
If the cause is amal katheer, then even a hafiz's prayer is invalidated because he performs extra actions. If the cause is talaqqun, then a hafiz's recitation is attributed to memory, not to the mus-haf, so his prayer is valid.
This explains the difference between the absolute view and the differentiated view.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Later authorities like al-Sarakhsi and Abu Nasr al-Saffar preferred the view that the hafiz's prayer is not invalidated. The mufta bihi is that only a non-hafiz's prayer is invalidated when reading from the mus-haf.
See Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihaya, and al-Tabyin.
5
Apply the tashabbuh principle
The passage ends with a note on imitation of the People of the Book. Not all imitation is disliked; only blameworthy and intended imitation is forbidden. This is a side issue but relevant to the context of early Muslims distinguishing their practices.
This clarifies that the ruling is not about imitation but about the act itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المحراب فسدت كما هو مقتضى الوجه الثاني كما صرحوا به وأطلقه فشمل القليل والكثير وما إذا لم يكن حافظاً أو حافظاً للقرآن وهو إطلاق الجامع الصغير، وذهب بعضهم إلى أنه إنما تفسد إذا قرأ آيه وبعضهم إذا قرأ الفاتحة. وقال الرازي قول أبي حنيفة محمول على من لم يحفظ القرآن ولا يمكنه أن يقرأ إلا من مصحف، فأما الحافظ فلا تفسد صلاته في قولهم جميعاً وتبعه على ذلك السرخسي في جامعه الصغير على ما في النهاية وأبو نصر الصفار على ما في الذخيرة معللاً بأن هذه القراءة مضافة إلى حفظه لا إلى تلقنه من المصحف، وجزم به في فتح القدير والنهاية والتبيين وهو أوجه كما لا يخفى. وفي الظهيرية : ثم لم يذكر في الكتاب أنه إذا لم يكن قادراً إلا على القراءة من المصحف فصلى بغير قراءة هل تجوز والأصح أنها لا تجوز ا.هـ. ويخالفه ما في النهاية نقلاً عن مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وكان الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل يقول في التعليل لأبي حنيفة أجمعنا على أن الرجل إذا كان يمكنه أن يقرأ المصحف ولا يمكنه أن يقرأ على ظهر قلبه أنه لو صلى بغير قراءة أنه يجزئه، ولو كانت المصحف جائزة لما أبيحت الصلاة بغير قراءة ولكن الظاهر أنهما لا يسلمان هذه قال بعض المشايخ ا.هـ. والظاهر أن ما في الظهيرية متفرع على أن علة الفساد حمله والعمل الكثير فإذا لم يحفظ شيئاً على ظهر قلبه يمكنه أن يقرأ من المصحف وهو موضوع فليس أمياً لتجوز صلاته بغير قراءة، وما ذكره الإمام الفضلي متفرع على الصحيح من أن علة الفساد تلقنه ولو كان موضوعاً فحينئذ لا قدرة له على القراءة فكان أمياً، وبهذا ظهر أن تصحيح الظهيرية مفرع على الضعيف. وأطلق في المصلي فشمل الإمام والمنفرد، فما في الهداية من تقييده بالإمام اتفاقي كما في غاية البيان. ثم اعلم أن التشبيه بأهل الكتاب لا يكره في كل شيء فإنا نأكل ونشرب كما يفعلون إنما الحرام هو التشبه فيما كان مذموماً وفيما يقصد به التشبيه كذا ذكره قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير فعلى هذا لو لم يقصد التشبه لا يكره عندهما .
The prayer is invalidated [when one reads from the mus-haf at the mihrab] as required by the second aspect, as they explained. He made it absolute, including little and much, and whether one is a hafiz or not; this is the absolute statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Some went to it being invalidated only if he reads a verse, some if he reads al-Fatiha. Al-Razi said: Abu Hanifa's statement is applied to one who does not memorize the Quran and cannot recite except from a mus-haf. As for the hafiz, his prayer is not invalidated in all of their statements. Al-Sarakhsi in his Jami' al-Saghir followed him, as in al-Nihaya, and Abu Nasr al-Saffar as in al-Dhakhira, reasoning that this recitation is attributed to his memory, not to his learning from the mus-haf. It is affirmed in Fath al-Qadir, al-Nihaya, and al-Tabyin, and it is more appropriate, as is not hidden. In al-Zahiriyya: Then he did not mention in the book that if he is only able to recite from the mus-haf and prays without recitation, is it permissible? The correct view is that it is not permissible. End. It contradicts what is in al-Nihaya quoting from the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. The Shaykh al-Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said in the reasoning for Abu Hanifa: We all agree that if a man can read the mus-haf but cannot recite from memory, his prayer without recitation is valid. If reading from the mus-haf were permissible, prayer without recitation would not be permitted, but apparently they both do not accept this, as some mashayikh said. End. It appears that what is in al-Zahiriyya is based on the cause of invalidity being carrying and excessive action, so if one memorizes nothing from the heart and can recite from the mus-haf while it is placed, he is not unlettered to permit his prayer without recitation. What Imam al-Fadli mentioned is based on the sound view that the cause of invalidity is learning from the mus-haf even if placed, then he has no ability to recite, so he is unlettered. Thus it becomes clear that the correction in al-Zahiriyya is based on the weak view. He made it absolute regarding the one praying, including the imam and the individual. So what is in al-Hidaya restricting it to the imam is merely incidental, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. Then know that imitation of the People of the Book is not disliked in everything; indeed we eat and drink as they do. Only the imitation that is blameworthy and intended for imitation is forbidden. Thus Qadi Khan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. Based on this, if one does not intend imitation, it is not disliked according to them.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether reading from the mus-haf (physical copy of the Quran) during prayer invalidates the prayer. The author starts by stating the ruling that if one reads from the mus-haf placed in the mihrab, the prayer is invalidated, based on the second of two opinions (الوجه الثاني). This is made absolute, applying whether little or much is read, and whether the person is a hafiz (memorizer of Quran) or not. However, some scholars differentiate: some say it only invalidates if a full verse is read, some say if al-Fatiha is read. Al-Razi reports that Abu Hanifa's statement is to be applied to one who does not memorize the Quran, so for a hafiz the prayer is not invalidated. This is followed by al-Sarakhsi and others, reasoning that the hafiz's recitation is based on memory, not on learning from the mus-haf. But the text from al-Zahiriyya says that if a person cannot recite except from the mus-haf and prays without recitation, the correct view is that it is not permissible (i.e., his prayer is invalid). This is contradictory to the view from al-Nihaya quoting Shaykh al-Islam Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, who says that Abu Hanifa and others agree that such a person's prayer without recitation is valid. The author reconciles by explaining that the cause of invalidity differs: some say the cause is carrying the mus-haf and performing excessive action (عمل كثير), while others say it is the act of learning/reciting from the mus-haf (تلقن). The first view makes the person unlettered (أمي) if he cannot recite from memory, so his prayer without recitation is valid. The second view makes him still capable of reciting from the mus-haf, so his prayer without recitation is invalid. The author notes that the correction in al-Zahiriyya is based on the weaker view. The passage then expands to include both imam and individual in the ruling. Finally, it adds a note about imitation of the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab) in actions, clarifying that not all imitation is disliked; only blameworthy and intentionally imitative actions are prohibited, based on Qadi Khan's commentary.

Key Terms
المصحف (al-mushaf): A physical copy of the Quran, as opposed to recitation from memory.
الحافظ (al-haafiz): A person who has memorized the entire Quran and can recite it from memory.
التشبيه بأهل الكتاب (al-tashabbuh bi ahl al-kitaab): Imitating the People of the Book (Jews and Christians) in their practices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, does reading from the mushaf invalidate the prayer of a hafiz?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, because his recitation is from memory, not from the mushaf.
C) Only if he reads more than one verse.
D) Only if he is the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on reading from the mus-haf during prayer depends on the cause of invalidation; for a hafiz, the prayer remains valid because his recitation is from memory.

Eating and Drinking During Prayer: The Principle of 'Amal Katheer
Ruling on invalidation of prayer by eating and drinking, with analysis of 'amal katheer and consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating and drinking during prayer, apply the distinction between large and small amounts, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding returning vomit.

Core Idea
Eating and drinking invalidate prayer only if they constitute excessive action ('amal katheer); a small amount is excused.

In this lesson, we examine the well-known ruling that eating and drinking invalidate the prayer. The key is not the act itself but the amount: a large amount is considered 'amal katheer (excessive action) and invalidates, while a small amount does not. This distinction is based on consensus (ijma') and is further refined by examples of what constitutes 'amal katheer. We also explore an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad concerning intentionally returning vomit during prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The matn states that eating and drinking invalidate the prayer. The reason given is that each is 'amal katheer (excessive action), which is not part of the prayer and not necessary.
The ruling is absolute in the matn but later qualified by consensus.
2
Define 'amal katheer
Qadi Khan defines 'amal katheer as action involving the hand, mouth, and tongue simultaneously. This is the benchmark for determining whether an act invalidates prayer.
This definition helps distinguish between large and small actions.
3
Distinguish between large and small amounts
The passage explicitly states that there is consensus (ijma') that a large amount (katheer) invalidates, while a small amount (qaleel) does not, because one can avoid large actions but not small natural movements.
Examples include a sesame seed (small, does not invalidate) vs. a mouthful (large, invalidates).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on returning vomit
Abu Yusuf holds that intentionally returning vomit during prayer does not invalidate, while Imam Muhammad holds it does. This difference is based on qiyas with fasting.
This shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh and the method of tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والأكل والشرب) أي يفسدانها لأن كل واحد منهما عمل كثير وليس من أعمال الصلاة ولا ضرورة إليه وعلل قاضيخان وجه كونه كثيراً بقوله : لأنه عمل اليد والفم واللسان. قال العلامة الحلبي : وهو مشكل بالنسبة إلى ما لو أخذ من خارج سمسمة فابتلعها أو وقع في فيه قطرة مطر فابتلعها فإنهم نصوا على فساد الصلاة في كل من هذه الصور مطلقاً ا هـ. أطلقه فشمل العمد والنسيان لأن حالة الصلاة مذكرة فلا يعفى النسيان بخلاف الصوم فإنه لا مذكر فيه. وشمل القليل والكثير ولهذا فسره في الحاوي بقدر ما يصل إلى الحلق، وقيده الشارح بما يفسد الصوم وما لا يفسد الصوم لا يبطل الصلاة ا هـ . وهو ممنوع كلياً فإنه لو ابتلع شيئاً بين أسنانه وكان قدر الحمصة لا تفسد صلاته وفي الصوم يفسد. وفرق بينهما الولوالجي وصاحب المحيط بأن فساد الصلاة معلق بعمل كثير ولم يوجد بخلاف فساد الصوم فإنه معلق بوصول المغذي إلى جوفه لكن في البدائع والخلاصة أنه لا فرق بين الصلاة والصوم في قدر الحمصة وفي الظهيرية : لو ابتلع دما خرج من بين أسنانه لم تفسد صلاته إذا لم يكن ملء الفم | وقالوا في باب الصوم: لو خرج من بين أسنانه دم ودخل وهو صائم إن كان الغلبة للدم أو كانا سواء فطره لأن له حكم الخارج، وإن كانت حلقه اهـ. : فساد الغلبة للبراق لا يضره كما في الوضوء فقد فرقوا بين الصلاة والصوم. وفي الظهيرية : لو قاء أقل من ملء الفم فعاد إلى جوفه وهو لا يملك إمساكه لم تفسد صلاته، وإن أعاده إلى جوفه وهو قادر على أن يمجه يجب أن يكون على قياس الصوم عند أبي يوسف لا تفسد، وعند محمد تفسد. وإن تقيأ في صلاته إن كان أقل من ملء الفم لا تفسد، وإن كان ملء الفم تفسد صلاته ا هـ . وفي المحيط وغيره: ولو مضغ العلك كثيراً فسدت، وكذا لو كان في فمه إهليلجة فلاكها فإن دخل في حلقه منها شيء يسير من غير أن يلوكها لا تفسد وإن كثر ذلك فسدت. وفي الخلاصة : ولو أكل شيئاً من الحلاوة وابتلع عينها فدخل في الصلاة فوجد حلاوتها في فيه ابتلعها لا تفسد صلاته ولو دخل الفانيد أو السكر في فيه ولم يمضغه لكن يصلي والحلاوة تصل إلى جوفه تفسد صلاته ا هـ. وأشار بالأكل والشرب إلى أن كل عمل كثير فهو مفسد، واتفقوا على أن الكثير مفسد والقليل لا لإمكان الاحتراز عن الكثير دون القليل فإن في الحي حركات من الطبع وليست من الصلاة فلو اعتبر العمل مفسداً مطلقاً لزم الخرج في إقامة صحتها وهو مدفوع بالنص .
His statement: (And eating and drinking) meaning they invalidate it (prayer), because each of them is a large amount of action (amal katheer) and is not from the actions of prayer, nor is there necessity for it. Qadi Khan explained the aspect of it being a large amount by saying: because it is action of the hand, mouth, and tongue. Al-Allama al-Halabi said: This is problematic with regard to one who takes a sesame seed from outside and swallows it, or a drop of rain falls into his mouth and he swallows it, for they explicitly ruled that the prayer is invalidated in all these cases absolutely. End. He made it absolute, including intentional and forgetful, because the state of prayer is a reminder, so forgetfulness is not excused, unlike fasting where there is no reminder. It includes little and much; for this reason he interpreted it in al-Hawi as the amount that reaches the throat. The commentator restricted it to that which invalidates fasting; what does not invalidate fasting does not invalidate prayer. End. This is completely rejected, because if he swallows something between his teeth the size of a chickpea, his prayer is not invalidated, but in fasting it invalidates. Al-Walwaliji and the author of al-Muhit differentiated between them: the invalidation of prayer is dependent on a large amount of action, which is not found, unlike the invalidation of fasting, which is dependent on the arrival of nourishment to his stomach. But in al-Bada'i' and al-Khulasa, there is no difference between prayer and fasting regarding the size of a chickpea. In al-Zahiriyya: If he swallows blood that came out from between his teeth, his prayer is not invalidated if it is not mouthful. And they said in the chapter of fasting: If blood comes out from between his teeth and enters while he is fasting, if the blood is dominant or equal, it breaks his fast because it has the ruling of what comes out. And if the saliva is dominant, it does not harm him, as in wudu. So they differentiated between prayer and fasting. In al-Zahiriyya: If he vomits less than a mouthful and it returns to his stomach while he cannot hold it back, his prayer is not invalidated. If he returns it to his stomach while he is able to expel it, analogically to fasting according to Abu Yusuf it is not invalidated, and according to Muhammad it invalidates. If he vomits in his prayer, if it is less than a mouthful, it does not invalidate; if it is a mouthful, it invalidates his prayer. End. In al-Muhit and others: If he chews gum excessively, his prayer is invalidated. So too if he had an eleocarpus fruit in his mouth and chewed it; if a little of it enters his throat without chewing, it does not invalidate; if it is a lot, it invalidates. In al-Khulasa: If he eats some candy and swallows it, then enters prayer and finds its sweetness in his mouth and swallows it, his prayer is not invalidated. If sugar candy or sugar enters his mouth, and he does not chew it but prays while the sweetness reaches his stomach, his prayer is invalidated. End. He indicated by eating and drinking that every large amount of action invalidates. And they agreed that a large amount invalidates and a small amount does not, because it is possible to avoid a large amount but not a small amount, for in a living being there are natural movements not from prayer. So if action were considered invalidating absolutely, it would lead to difficulty in establishing its validity, and that is rebutted by the text (nass).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on eating and drinking during prayer. The author (the commentator) expands on the statement in the matn that 'eating and drinking invalidate the prayer'. The reasoning is that each is a 'large amount of action' (amal katheer), not from the actions of prayer, and there is no necessity for it. Qadi Khan explains that it is large because it involves the hand, mouth, and tongue. However, al-Halabi points out a problem: if one swallows a small sesame seed or a raindrop, scholars still rule that it invalidates prayer absolutely. The ruling includes intentional and forgetful acts, because prayer is a state of remembrance and forgetfulness is not excused, unlike fasting. It includes both little and much amounts; but some restrict it to the amount that reaches the throat. The commentator (the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq) criticizes the view that only that which invalidates fasting invalidates prayer, giving the example of a chickpea-sized piece between teeth: it does not invalidate prayer but invalidates fasting. Al-Walwaliji and al-Muhit differentiate: prayer invalidation is due to excessive action, which is not found in a small piece; fasting invalidation is due to nutrition reaching the stomach. However, al-Bada'i' and al-Khulasa say there is no difference. The passage then gives further examples: swallowing blood from between teeth, vomiting, chewing gum, swallowing candy, etc. The general principle is that a large amount of action invalidates, and there is consensus (ittifaaq) that a large amount invalidates while a small amount does not, because one can avoid large actions but not small natural movements. This, they say, is supported by the primary texts (nass).

Key Terms
العمل الكثير (al-'amal al-katheer): Excessive movement during prayer that is not part of the prayer and cannot be ignored, typically defined as a movement that occupies both hands or more than one limb.
ملء الفم (mal' al-fam): A mouthful; used as a measure: if something (like blood or vomit) fills the mouth, it is considered a large amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the consensus (ijma) mentioned in the passage, which of the following invalidates prayer?
A) Swallowing a sesame seed while praying
B) Swallowing a large mouthful of water while praying
C) Getting a drop of rain in the mouth and swallowing it unintentionally
D) Tasting food without swallowing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that eating or drinking invalidates prayer only if it constitutes a large amount of action ('amal katheer); small amounts are excused, and this is supported by ijma.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Eating and Drinking in Prayer and the Definition of Much Action
Commentary on the ruling and definition dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that eating and drinking invalidate prayer, identify the two definitions of 'much action', and explain why the observer test is preferred.

Core Idea
Much action invalidates prayer; the observer's certainty defines what is 'much'.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling that eating and drinking invalidate prayer, but with a crucial nuance: only 'significant' amounts matter. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the definition of amal kathir, presenting two competing views within the school. We will examine the evidence for each and see why the observer test was chosen as the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Eating and drinking invalidate prayer because they are amal kathir (significant actions) foreign to the acts of prayer.
This is the starting point agreed upon in the school.
2
Understand the scope of the ruling
The ruling covers both intentional and forgetful acts, and both little and much, but exceptions exist for tiny amounts (e.g., a sesame seed).
Forgetfulness is not excused because prayer constantly reminds the worshipper.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on defining 'much'
Two definitions: (1) Observer test: an action that an observer (who does not know the person is praying) has no doubt is not prayer is 'much'. (2) Two-hand/one-hand test: what is normally done with two hands is 'much', even if done with one hand; what is done with one hand is 'little'.
The observer test is also called the 'asahh' (most correct) view.
4
Evaluate the critique of the two-hand test
Chewing gum and eating/drinking are done with one hand yet invalidate by agreement, contradicting the two-hand rule. Examples like oiling hair or combing beard also fail the test.
This critique shows the two-hand test is not comprehensive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The observer test is chosen because it accommodates all cases, including gum chewing and eating. It is declared 'asahh' by al-Bada'i and 'ahsan' by al-Muhit.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

His saying: (And eating and drinking) means they invalidate it because each of them is a significant action and not from the actions of prayer and there is no necessity for it. Qadikhan explained the aspect of it being significant by saying: because it is an action of the hand, mouth, and tongue. Allamah Halabi said: This is problematic with respect to if he takes a sesame seed from outside and swallows it, or a drop of rain falls into his mouth and he swallows it, for they explicitly ruled that prayer is invalidated in each of these cases absolutely. He said it absolutely, so it includes intentional and forgetful, because the state of prayer is a reminder, so forgetfulness is not excused unlike fasting where there is no reminder. And it includes little and much, and for this reason he interpreted in al-Hawi as what reaches the throat, and the commentator restricted it to what invalidates fasting and what does not invalidate fasting does not invalidate prayer. This is totally rejected, because if he swallows something between his teeth the size of a chickpea, his prayer is not invalidated, while in fasting it invalidates. Al-Walwalji and the author of al-Muhit distinguished between them: invalidation of prayer is dependent on a significant action, which is not found, unlike invalidation of fasting which is dependent on nutritive substance reaching the stomach. But in al-Bada'i and al-Khulasa, there is no difference between prayer and fasting regarding the size of a chickpea. And in al-Zahiriyya: If he swallows blood that came out from between his teeth, his prayer is not invalidated if it is not mouthful. And they said in the chapter on fasting: If blood comes out from between his teeth and enters while he is fasting, if the blood prevails or they are equal, it breaks his fast because it has the ruling of that which exits, and if the saliva prevails, it does not harm him as in wudu. So they distinguished between prayer and fasting. And in al-Zahiriyya: If he vomits less than a mouthful and it returns to his stomach and he cannot control it, his prayer is not invalidated. If he returns it to his stomach while able to expectorate, it must be on analogy with fasting: according to Abu Yusuf it does not invalidate, according to Muhammad it invalidates. If he vomits in his prayer, if less than a mouthful it does not invalidate, if a mouthful it invalidates. And in al-Muhit and others: If he chews gum excessively it invalidates, and similarly if he has a myrobalan in his mouth and chews it, if a little enters his throat without chewing, it does not invalidate, but if it becomes much it invalidates. In al-Khulasa: If he eats some sweet and swallows its substance, then enters prayer and finds its sweetness in his mouth and swallows it, his prayer is not invalidated. But if rock candy or sugar enters his mouth and he does not chew it, but prays while the sweetness reaches his stomach, his prayer is invalidated. And by eating and drinking he indicated that every significant action is invalidating. And they agreed that much invalidates and little does not, because it is possible to avoid much but not little, for in a living being there are natural movements not part of prayer; if action were considered invalidating absolutely, it would lead to difficulty in establishing its validity, and this is repelled by the text. To the point that the form of similarity in what concerns the welfare of people does not harm, and this type of ruling concerns the welfare of people, for the land cannot be traversed over long distances except with this type of ruling. His saying: (But in al-Bada'i and al-Khulasa there is a correction to what preceded, useful for repelling the objection. His saying: (And in al-Zahiriyya, if he swallowed blood that came out from between his teeth) is absolute here, and the detail later is that there is no difference between the prevailing and the prevailed, but if it is [PAGE 20] Book of Prayer, Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Prayer. Then they differed regarding what determines much and little on several opinions. One of them is what the general scholars chose, as in al-Khulasa and al-Khaniyya: every action that the observer has no doubt is not in prayer is much, and every action that the observer is uncertain whether the doer is in prayer is little. He said in al-Bada'i: This is most correct. And the commentator and al-Walwalji followed him. And in al-Muhit he said: It is the best. And al-Sadr al-Shahid said: It is the correct view. And Allamah Halabi mentioned that apparently they mean by 'observer' one who does not know of the worshipper's commencement in prayer; then if he sees him in this action and is certain he is not in prayer, it is a significant action, and if he doubts, it is little. The second: what is normally done with two hands is much, even if one does it with one hand, like wrapping a turban, wearing a shirt, tightening trousers, shooting a bow; and what is done with one hand is little, even if done with two hands, like removing a shirt, loosening trousers, putting on a cap and taking it off, removing a bridle, and similar. Thus mentioned by the commentator, and he did not restrict in al-Khulasa and al-Khaniyya what is done with two hands by custom. And he restricted in al-Khaniyya what is done with one hand to when it is not repeated, and repetition means three consecutive times, as in al-Khulasa: If he scratches three times in one pillar, his prayer is invalidated. This is if he raises his hand each time; if he does not raise his hand each time, it does not invalidate because it is one scratch. This is a strange restriction and wonderful detail deserving to be memorized. But in al-Zahiriyya, attributed to al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din: If he scratches a spot on his body three times in one go, his prayer is invalidated. And I have not seen anyone who authenticated the second opinion on determining action, and it may be said it is not correct. And if he chews gum in his prayer, his prayer is invalidated, as mentioned by Muhammad in al-Bada'i, because an observer from a distance has no doubt that he is not in prayer, and there is no use of hands at all, let alone use of both hands. Similarly, eating and drinking are done with one hand and are invalidating by agreement. Similarly, their saying: if he oils his head or combs his hair, whether hair of head or beard, his prayer is invalidated, cannot be derived from the view that much action is what is done with two hands, because oiling head and combing hair are normally done with one hand, unless by oiling he means taking the bottle and pouring oil from it with the other hand, which is so, for in al-Muhit he said: And if he pours oil on his head, because it is usually from matters of preceding hadath, and it does not contradict non-invalidation. His saying: (And I have not seen anyone who authenticated the second opinion). Sheikh Ismail said after mentioning al-Durar: This second opinion is the choice of Sheikh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl. Thus in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa. And he presented it definitively in al-Majmu', and al-Atabi confined himself to it. And in 'Umdat al-Mufti, he then said: Rather the apparent meaning of what is in al-Hawi at the end of the subdivision supports it. His saying: (And it may be said it is not correct, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the condition of circumstance is considered; the meaning of 'what is done with two hands is much' is from the perspective that it is done with them. But on this, chewing gum remains of unknown ruling, and there is no impediment to considering something else in this opinion. His saying: (If he chews gum in his prayer, it invalidates, etc.) meaning if the chewing is excessive as in al-Tajnisi. His saying: (It is with one hand) will come. His saying: (Unless by oiling he means taking it, etc.) And the discussion remains.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling that eating and drinking invalidate prayer. The author begins by affirming that each is a 'significant action' (amal kathir) and not part of prayer. Qadikhan specifies it involves hand, mouth, and tongue. Al-Halabi problematizes this by noting that even a tiny sesame seed or raindrop, if swallowed, invalidates prayer absolutely—contradicting the idea that only 'significant' amounts matter. The text then explains that the ruling covers both intentional and forgetful acts because prayer constantly reminds the worshipper, unlike fasting. It also covers both little and much, though later distinctions arise. The commentator initially equates the invalidating amount with what invalidates fasting, but this is rejected because a chickpea-sized morsel between teeth does not invalidate prayer yet invalidates fasting. Al-Walwalji and al-Muhit distinguish: prayer invalidation requires a 'significant action' (not found in a small swallow), while fasting invalidation depends on nutritive substance reaching the stomach. However, al-Bada'i and al-Khulasa state no difference in quantity for chickpea-sized. Al-Zahiriyya reports that swallowing blood from gums does not invalidate prayer if less than a mouthful, whereas in fasting, blood and saliva are treated differently. Vomiting less than a mouthful that returns involuntarily does not invalidate; if voluntary, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ. Chewing gum excessively invalidates, but a tiny piece slipping down without chewing does not. The consensus is that 'much' invalidates, 'little' does not, because much can be avoided. The text then moves to defining 'much' and 'little'. There are two main opinions: (1) the observer test: an action that an observer has no doubt is not prayer is 'much'; if doubtful, 'little'. (2) what is normally done with two hands is 'much', with one hand is 'little'. The second opinion is illustrated with examples: wrapping a turban (two-handed) even if done with one hand, scratching three consecutive times (if hand raised each time) invalidates. But this is refined: if done in one go without raising hand, it is one action. The author notes that chewing gum and eating/drinking are done with one hand yet invalidate by agreement, undermining the second opinion. He concludes by citing authorities and noting that the second opinion is not universally authenticated.

Key Terms
الأكل والشرب (al-akl wa al-shurb): Eating and drinking, which invalidate prayer if they constitute a significant action (amal kathir).
عمل كثير (amal kathir): A significant action that invalidates prayer; defined by the observer test or customary practice.
الناظر (al-nazir): The observer who does not know the worshipper's intention; his certainty/doubt determines whether an action is 'much' or 'little'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred opinion in this passage, what determines whether an action is 'much' (kathir) and invalidates prayer?
A) Use of two hands vs. one hand
B) The action being repeated three consecutive times
C) Whether an observer who does not know the person is praying has no doubt that the person is not in prayer
D) Whether the action involves eating or drinking specifically

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'much action' by the observer test, relying on the principle that what can be avoided is invalidating, while unavoidable minor movements are excused.
