Looking at a Written Text in Prayer: Ruling and Dispute
Ruling on looking at a written text and understanding it while praying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a written text in prayer, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute over the mustafhim case, and explain the reasoning based on absence of recitation and shubhat al-ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Looking at writing in prayer does not invalidate, even if understood; prayer is valid but sinful if intentional without need.

This lesson examines the fiqh ruling when a person looks at a written text during prayer and understands its meaning. The Hanafi position distinguishes between mere looking and intended recitation, and an intra-madhhab dispute arises when the person seeks to understand (mustafhim). We will trace the evidence and the reliance on shubhat al-ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Find the key phrase: 'ولو نظر إلى مكتوب وفهمه' (if one looks at a written text and understands it). The ruling is 'لا تفسد' (it does not invalidate) but 'أثم' (sins) if intentional without need.
The text explicitly states the prayer is valid but sinful.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is an analogy with an oath: if one swears not to read a book, looking and understanding does not break the oath because the purpose is understanding, not recitation. For Quran, there is consensus (ijma) that it does not invalidate.
The dalil is based on the absence of physical recitation and the meaning-focused nature of the act.
3
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the person seeks to understand (mustafhim), the prayer invalidates because he is engaged in learning. The correct view (sahih) is that it does not, due to no physical act and shubhat al-ikhtilaf (suspicion of difference).
The dispute hinges on whether mental engagement counts as qira'ah (recitation) in the technical sense.
4
Note the Practical Admonition
Fuqaha advise that a jurist should not place a book before him during prayer to avoid falling into the area of dispute (shubhat al-ikhtilaf). Some texts even make it obligatory (wajib).
This is a precautionary measure, not a ruling of invalidation.
5
Distinguish from Related Rulings
The passage also mentions eating what is between the teeth and a passerby walking in front – both do not invalidate but are sinful. This shows a pattern: minor, non-recitational acts do not break prayer.
The general principle: only explicit speech or major external actions invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو نظر إلى مكتوب وفهمه أو أكل ما بين أسنانه أو مر مارّ في موضع سجوده لا تفسد وإن أثم أما الأوّل فلأن الفساد إنما يتعلق في مثله بالقراءة وبالنظر مع الفهم لم المصنف في الكافي أنه متفق عليه بخلاف من حلف لا يقرأ كتاب فلان تحصل، وصحح فنظر إليه وفهمه فإنه يحنث عنه محمد لأن المقصود فيه الفهم والوقوف على سره. أطلق المكتوب فشمل ما هو قرآن وغيره لكن في القرآن لا تفسد إجماعاً بالاتفاق كما في النهاية، وشمل ما إذا استفهم أو لا، لكن إذا لم يكن مستفهماً لا تفسد بالإجماع، وإن كان مستفهماً ففي المنية تفسد عند محمد والصحيح عدمه اتفاقاً لعدم الفعل منه ولشبهة الاختلاف قالوا : ينبغي للفقيه أن لا يضع جز تعليقه بين يديه في الصلاة لأنه ربما يقع بصره على ما في الجزء فيفهم ذلك فيدخل فيه شبهة الاختلاف ا.هـ. وعبر في النهاية بالوجوب على الفقيه أن لا يضع لكن قد علمت أن شبهة الاختلاف فيما إذا كان مستفهماً، وأما إذا لم يكن مستفهماً فلا يعلل بما ذكر لعدم الاختلاف فيه بل لاشتغال قلبه به إذا خاف من وضعه بين يديه اشتغاله بالنظر إليه ولم يذكروا كراهة النظر إلى المكتوب متعمداً، وفي منية المصلي ما يقتضيها فإنه قال : ولو أنشأ شعراً أو خطبة ولم يتكلم بلسانه لا تفسد وقد أساء، وعلل الإساءة شارحها تفسد صلاتها قوله : (وأما فسادها بتقديم الإمام أمام المصلي) كذا في النسخ والظاهر فيه تقديماً وتأخيراً من الناسخ وأصل العبارة بتقدم المصلي أمام الإمام.
His statement: (And if one looks at a written text and understands it, or eats what is between his teeth, or a passerby passes in the place of his prostration, it does not invalidate [the prayer] even if he sins. As for the first, invalidation in such a case is connected only to recitation, and to looking with understanding — [the author] in al-Kafi said it is agreed upon, unlike one who swears he will not read so-and-so's book; if he obtains it and looks at it and understands it, he has broken his oath according to Muhammad because the intended purpose is understanding and knowing its secret. 'Written text' is general, including Quran and other, but regarding Quran it does not invalidate by consensus as in al-Nihayah. It also includes whether he seeks to understand or not, but if he does not seek to understand, it does not invalidate by consensus. If he seeks to understand, then in al-Munyah it invalidates according to Muhammad, but the correct view is that it does not invalidate by agreement due to absence of an act from him and due to the suspicion of difference. They said: it is befitting for a jurist not to place a juz' of his compilation before him in prayer because maybe his eye will fall on what is in the juz' and he will understand it, thus entering into the suspicion of difference. End. In al-Nihayah, it is expressed as obligatory for the jurist not to place, but you know that the suspicion of difference is only when he seeks to understand; if he does not seek to understand, it is not reasoned by what was mentioned due to absence of difference in it, but rather due to his heart being occupied if he fears that placing it before him will occupy him by looking at it. They did not mention the dislike of intentionally looking at the written text. In Munyat al-Musalli, there is what indicates it: he said, 'If he composes poetry or a sermon and does not speak with his tongue, it does not invalidate but he has done wrong.' Its commentator explained the wrongness as it invalidating her prayer. His statement: (As for its invalidation by the imam going ahead of the one praying) — thus in the manuscripts, and apparently it is a transposition from the copyist, and the original phrase is 'by the one praying going ahead of the imam'.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the ruling of looking at a written text during prayer. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that it does not invalidate prayer even if the person sins. The commentator explains that invalidation would require both looking and understanding, and the text being something that can be recited. There is a distinction: if the text is Quran, all agree it does not invalidate because the act is not speech but thought. If the person is trying to understand (mustafhim), there is a dispute: Muhammad holds it invalidates, but the correct view (sahih) is that it does not, because there is no actual speech and minimal action. The commentator advises against placing a book before oneself to avoid the suspicion. A related ruling from Munyat al-Musalli compares composing poetry mentally: it does not invalidate but is wrong. The passage ends with a textual correction about the imam going ahead of the person praying, noting that the original author's wording was 'by the person praying going ahead of the imam'.

Key Terms
مستفهم (mustafhim): One who looks at a text with the intention to understand its meaning, not merely recitation.
شبهة الاختلاف (shubhat al-ikhtilaf): A situation where there is a difference of opinion among jurists, creating a suspicion that the act may be invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a person looks at a written text during prayer and understands it without reciting aloud?
A) The prayer is invalidated
B) The prayer is valid but sinful
C) The prayer is valid and not sinful
D) The prayer becomes makruh

Key Takeaway
Looking at a written text and understanding it does not invalidate prayer, but intentionally doing so without need is sinful; the relied-upon view overrides the minority intra-Hanafi dispute.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Swallowing Food Remnants in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on swallowing food remnants during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on swallowing food remnants during prayer and identify the condition (chewing) that leads to consensus on invalidation.

Core Idea
Swallowing remnants without chewing may not invalidate prayer; the amount threshold is disputed among Hanafis.

You might think that any eating during prayer invalidates it. But what if you have a tiny piece of food stuck between your teeth from before prayer? The Hanafi school has three detailed opinions on this. This lesson unpacks them and shows where there is agreement and where there is continued dispute among later authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default classification
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq classifies eating what is between teeth as a 'little action' ('amal qalil). Understand that little actions generally do not invalidate prayer unless they meet the threshold of 'amal kathir.
The default is that little action is excused; the dispute is about what counts as little.
2
List the three Hanafi opinions on the amount
Opinion 1 (al-Bada'i', Sharh al-Tahawi): If the amount is a chickpea (himmasa) or more, prayer is invalidated; less does not. Opinion 2 (Khuwahar Zadeh in al-Khulasah): Only if it is a mouthful (mil'u al-fam) does it invalidate. Opinion 3: Some tie invalidation to the definition of 'amal kathir, with no fixed amount.
Each opinion uses a different measure: chickpea, mouthful, or the general concept of 'much action'.
3
Note the consensus on chewing
The passage states clearly that if the remnants are chewed, there is no dispute: the prayer is invalidated regardless of amount. This is analogous to chewing gum during prayer.
Chewing transforms the act from passive swallowing to active eating, which is always 'amal kathir.
4
Evaluate the preponderant view
The commentator leans toward the view that swallowing without chewing and less than a chickpea does not invalidate. He notes that the definition of 'amal kathir is the basis for tarjih, and invites further examination (falyatamallal).
The preponderant view is that little action without chewing is excused; the chickpea rule from al-Muhit may be a later fatwa.

ترجيح القول الأول ومقتضى هذا أنه لو ابتلع ما فوق الحمصة بدون مضغ يكون الأصح عدم الفساد فليتأمل هذا. وفي الشرنبلالية قال بعد ذكره قول المؤلف وهو يبني الخ: وفيه تأمل لأن القائل بأن ملء الفم يفسد وكذا نحوه لا يشترط معه العمل الكثير بل علته إمكان الاحتراز عنه بلا كلفة بخلاف القليل لكونه تبعاً لريقه فلا يفسد إلا بالعمل الكثير وفي معرفته الاختلاف المعلوم ا واعترضه الرملي أيضاً بأنه لا يتجه ذلك مع As for the second, i.e., eating what is between his teeth, it is because it is a little action. He (the author) made it absolute, so it includes if it is the amount of a chickpea as we have presented from al-Muhit and al-Walwajijiyyah regarding prayer and fasting. In al-Bada'i': if it is less than a chickpea, it does not harm him; if it is the amount of a chickpea or more, his prayer is invalidated. Similarly in Sharh al-Tahawi. And some said: his prayer is not invalidated by what is less than a mouthful. So these are three opinions on this issue as you see, and the concern is which is the most preponderant (rajih). It depends on knowing 'amal kathir (much action), and there is difference on this as previously. His statement: (And it depends on knowing much action) I say: perhaps the preponderance of the first opinion follows, and the implication of this is that if he swallows more than a chickpea without chewing, the correct view would be no invalidation, so let this be examined. In al-Shurnublaliyyah, after mentioning the author's statement that it depends, he said: There is consideration because the one who says that a mouthful invalidates and the like does not require much action with it; rather its cause is the possibility of avoiding it without difficulty, unlike the little since it is a consequence of his saliva, so it does not invalidate except with much action, and the known difference in its definition. al-Ramli objected to this also saying that it is not consistent with their explicit statement that prayer is invalidated by swallowing a sesame seed taken from outside or a drop of water that fell into his mouth since they did not tie invalidation to that, and similarly if there was sugar or candy in his mouth and he swallowed its solution. His statement: (As for if he chewed it a lot) al-Ramli said: i.e., by consecutive three chews as in Sharh al-Munyah for al-Halabi. End. I say: the lack of estimating it by three may be specific to that third opinion. His statement: (And upon this...) He said in al-Nahr: There is discussion; if it is settled that little action does not invalidate, and there is no doubt that less than a chickpea is free from needing much chewing, indeed chewing cannot occur for it due to its dissolution between the teeth, so it does not invalidate, unlike the chickpea. End. I say: the author's speech is when he chews it a lot, and that does not contradict it being free from needing chewing, and the claim that chewing cannot occur for it is subject to prevention, for chewing according to al-Qamus...

Commentary
This passage delves into a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding swallowing food remnants from between the teeth during prayer. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq stated it does not invalidate, but the commentator examines three opinions: (1) If the amount is a chickpea (himmasa) or more, it invalidates; less does not. (2) If less than a mouthful, it does not invalidate. (3) Some link invalidation to 'amal kathir (much action). The discussion includes important conditions: if the food is chewed, there is consensus it invalidates (like chewing gum); if swallowed without chewing, it may not invalidate if the amount is small. The passage also engages with later scholars like al-Ramli, noting contradictions: if a sesame seed from outside invalidates, why not remnants? The author suggests that swallowing without chewing is the locus of difference. The passage concludes with a discussion on the definition of chewing and its impact, referencing al-Qamus. The overall aim is to determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, which seems to favor no invalidation for small amounts without chewing, but the issue remains nuanced.

Key Terms
الحمصة (al-himmisa): The amount of a chickpea, used as a threshold for determining whether eating invalidates prayer.
ملء الفم (mil'u al-fam): A mouthful; a measure used in some opinions to indicate the amount that invalidates prayer.
العمل الكثير (al-'amal al-kathir): Much action that distracts from prayer and invalidates it; its definition is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) If the food is chewed, regardless of the amount
D) If the food is swallowed without chewing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal differences on swallowing remnants in prayer, but there is consensus that chewing anything during prayer invalidates it.

The Ruling on Eating During Salah: Amount that Invalidates
Explaining three opinions on eating during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the amount of eating that invalidates prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Eating a chickpea or more invalidates prayer; less is disliked, but chewing any amount invalidates.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we explore the precise ruling on eating during salah. While it is generally prohibited to engage in extraneous actions, the Hanafi school has three detailed opinions on the threshold. This lesson will clarify these positions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal act (eating during prayer) and its default hukm: it is an extraneous action that can invalidate if above a threshold.
The ruling depends on amount and manner (chewing vs. swallowing).
2
List the three intra-Hanafi opinions
From the text: (1) Al-Bada'i': chickpea-sized or more invalidates. (2) Some: only a mouthful invalidates. (3) Khwaharzadah: pre-existing food in mouth does not invalidate unless a mouthful.
The disagreement hinges on the definition of amal kathir.
3
Understand the basis: amal kathir
Each opinion ties invalidation to the concept of 'many actions' (amal kathir). The chickpea view links it to a measurable amount; the mouthful view to a larger quantity; Khwaharzadah considers the action is not truly voluntary.
Amal kathir is a contested concept within the school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The author leans towards the chickpea opinion, especially when the food is chewed. This is more relied upon in later fatwa practice.
Other opinions are considered weaker but still valid.
5
Note the practical consequence
The difference affects whether a person must repeat the prayer or simply avoid the action. Knowing the threshold helps in daily practice.
The ruling applies only to deliberate eating; forgetfulness requires sajdah sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها

الفرق
باشتغالة بما ليس من أعمال الصلاة من غير ضرورة قال : ثم ينبغي أن يكون عليه سجود السهو إذا أشغله ذلك عن أداء ركن أو واجب سهواً ا هـ. وبهذا علم أن ترك الخشوع لا يخل بالصحة بل بالكمال ولذا قال في الخلاصة والخانية إذا تفكر في صلاته فتذكر شعراً أو خطبة فقرأهما بقلبه ولم يتكلم بلسانه لا تفسد صلاته ا هـ. وأما الثاني وهو أسنانة أكله بین فلأنه عمل قليل، أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان قدر الحمصة كما قدمناه عن المحيط والوالجية من بين الصلاة والصوم. وفي البدائع : إن كان دون الحمصة لم يضره وإن كان قدر الحمصة فصاعداً فسدت صلاته، وهكذا في شرح الطحاوي. وقال بعضهم : لا تفسد صلاته بما دون ملء الفم وعليه مشى في الخلاصة حيث قال : وقال الإمام خواهر زاده : ولو أكل بعض اللقمة وبقي البعض في فيه حتى شرع في الصلاة وابتلع الباقي لا تفسد صلاته ما لم يكن ملء الفم. فهذه ثلاثة أقوال في هذه المسألة كما ترى والشأن فيما هو الراجح منها وهو ينبني على معرفة العمل الكثير وفيه اختلاف كما سبق، وينبغي أن يكون محل الاختلاف فيما إذا ابتلع ما بين أسنانه من غير مضغ، أما إذا مضغه فلا خلاف في فسادها كما قدمنا في مضغ العلك، وعلى هذا فلو عبر المصنف بالابتلاع كما في أ الخلاصة والمحيط والولوالجية وكثير دون الأكل لكان أولى ثم إذا كان ابتلاع ما بين أسنانه غير مفسد بشرطه على الخلاف
هـ.
أنه
وتأخيراً من الناسخ وأصل العبارة بتقدم المصلي أمام الإمام قوله : (قال) ثم ينبغي أن يكون عليه سجود السهو الخ) قال الشيخ اسمعيل لي فيه نظر لأنه إن فات الركن بالكلية فلا فائدة في السجود لكونه لا يجزئ عنه، وإن لم يفت فسجود السهو عليه لتأخير الركن عن محله مقرر كما يأتي وكلامه يوهم ا بحث منه قوله : (وهو ينبني على معرفة العمل الكثير) أقول قد يسبق ترجيح القول الأول ومقتضى هذا أنه لو ابتلع ما فوق الحمصة بدون مضغ يكون الأصح عدم الفساد فليتأمل هذا. وفي الشرنبلالية قال بعد ذكره قول المؤلف وهو يبني الخ: وفيه تأمل لأن القائل بأن ملء الفم يفسد وكذا نحوه لا يشترط معه العمل الكثير بل علته إمكان الاحتراز عنه بلا كلفة بخلاف القليل لكونه تبعاً لريقه فلا يفسد إلا بالعمل الكثير وفي معرفته الاختلاف المعلوم ا واعترضه الرملي أيضاً بأنه لا يتجه ذلك مع تصريحهم بفسادها بابتلاع سمسمة تناولها من خارج وقطرة ماء وقعت في فمه إذا لم ينيطوا في ذلك الفساد به، وكذا لو كان في فمه سكر أو فانيد وابتلع ذوبه قوله : (إما إذا مضغه كثيراً) قال الرملي : أي بأن توالت ثلاث مضغات كما في شرح المنية للحلبي .ا.هـ. قلت: عدم تقديره بالثلاث ربما يختص بذلك بالقول الثالث قوله : (وعلى هذا الخ قال في النهر : فيه بحث إذا قد تقرر أن العمل القليل لا يفسد، ولا شك أن ما دون الحمصة غني عن الكثير من المضغ بل لا يتأتى فيه مضغ لتلاشيه بين الأسنان فلا يفسد بخلاف الحمصة ا هـ . قلت : كلام المؤلف فيما إذا مضغه كثيراً ولا ينافيه كونه غنياً عن المضغ، ودعوى عدم تأتي المضغ فيه في حيز المنع فإن المضغ على ما في القاموس

The book of prayer, chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. 25. The difference: By occupying oneself with what is not from the actions of prayer without necessity. Likewise if there is sugar or candy in his mouth and he swallowed its melt. He said: (As if he chewed it much) Al-Ramli said: i.e., by three consecutive chews as in Sharh al-Munya by al-Halabi, end. I say: Not limiting it to three perhaps is specific to the third opinion. He said: (Upon this... Al-Nahr said: There is discussion in it since it has been established that a small action does not invalidate, and there is no doubt that what is less than a chickpea is independent of much chewing, rather chewing cannot occur in it because it disintegrates between the teeth, so it does not invalidate, unlike a chickpea, end. I say: The author's speech is regarding when he chewed it much, and it does not contradict it being independent of chewing, and the claim that chewing cannot occur in it is subject to denial, for chewing according to al-Qamus is... because... 26. The book of prayer, chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. So it is disliked as stated in Munyat al-Musalli because it is not from the actions of prayer and there is no necessity in it, so it is disliked even if little.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rules related to eating and swallowing during prayer. It begins by distinguishing between actions that invalidate prayer and those that are disliked. The author states that occupying oneself with anything not part of prayer without necessity can invalidate if it involves a large action, but if it involves forgetfulness, it may require prostrations of forgetfulness. The main focus is on eating during prayer. Three opinions are presented: first, from al-Bada'i' that if the amount is less than a chickpea it does not harm, but if it is a chickpea or more, prayer is invalidated. Second, that it does not invalidate unless it fills the mouth. Third, from Khwaharzadah that if part of a morsel is already in the mouth before prayer, swallowing it does not invalidate unless it is a mouthful. The text discusses the concept of 'amal kathir (many actions) as the key to determining invalidation. It also specifies that the disagreement applies to swallowing without chewing; if one chews, the prayer is invalidated even if the amount is small, due to the multiplicity of actions. Finally, the passage concludes that chewing even a small amount is disliked because it is not from the actions of prayer and there is no necessity.

Key Terms
عمل كثير (amal kathir): An action that involves multiple movements or significant physical activity, such as chewing or multiple swallows.
حمصة (himsa): A chickpea; used as a standard measure for the size of food that can invalidate prayer.
ابتلاع (ibtilā'): Swallowing, specifically of food remnants between teeth without chewing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person swallows a chickpea-sized food remnant that was between his teeth without chewing?
A) Prayer is invalidated according to all three opinions.
B) Prayer is valid because it is not a mouthful.
C) Prayer is invalidated according to the first opinion (chickpea) but valid according to the third opinion.
D) Prayer is valid because there was no chewing.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that eating a chickpea or more invalidates prayer, but less than that is only disliked, provided it is swallowed without chewing.

Chewing During Salah: The Principle of Amal Kathir
Analyzing the ruling on chewing during prayer and the principle of amal kathir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why chewing even a small amount of food invalidates prayer, applying the Hanafi principle of amal kathir.

Core Idea
Chewing is a multiplicity of actions (amal kathir) that invalidates prayer because of repetition.

This lesson delves into the second part of the passage, where the author distinguishes between swallowing without chewing (which may be forgiven) and chewing (which is universally invalidating). The key is the legal principle of amal kathir and how it applies to repetitive actions like chewing.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the distinction
The text explicitly separates swallowing from chewing. Swallowing without chewing may be subject to ikhtilaf, but chewing removes all disagreement.
The author states: 'أما إذا مضغه فلا خلاف في فسادها'.
2
Identify the principle: amal kathir
Chewing involves multiple movements (bites, grinds), which constitutes 'many actions' (amal kathir). This is the underlying legal reason for invalidation.
Amal kathir is a well-known concept in Hanafi fiqh; it is defined by the accumulation of movements.
3
Apply the principle to chewing
Even if the food amount is minimal, chewing makes the action multiple. Therefore, prayer is invalidated regardless of the quantity.
This is why the chickpea threshold is not applied when chewing occurs.
4
Note the threshold of chewing
The passage mentions that 'much chewing' is needed, and some define it as three consecutive chews (from al-Ramli). This further refines the concept.
Fewer than three chews might be considered amal qalil, but the text leans towards invalidation with any chewing.
5
Consider the exception
If food is less than a chickpea and disintegrates without actual chewing, it may not be considered amal kathir. The author points out that such a small amount 'is independent of much chewing'.
This is a nuance that shows the principle is not absolute but depends on the reality of the action.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rules related to eating and swallowing during prayer. It begins by distinguishing between actions that invalidate prayer and those that are disliked. The author states that occupying oneself with anything not part of prayer without necessity can invalidate if it involves a large action, but if it involves forgetfulness, it may require prostrations of forgetfulness. Finally, the passage concludes that chewing even a small amount is disliked because it is not from the actions of prayer and there is no necessity.

Key Terms
مضغ (madhgh): Chewing; the act of grinding food with teeth, which is considered a multiplicity of actions (amal kathir).
ثلاث مضغات (thalath madhghāt): Three consecutive chews; a threshold mentioned by al-Ramli as defining 'much chewing' (amal kathir).
العمل الكثير (al-amal al-kathir): The many actions; a legal principle that actions involving multiple movements invalidate prayer if done intentionally.

The Ruling on Prayer Validity When a Passerby Crosses
Clarifying non-invalidation and sin of passerby

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer is not invalidated by a passerby, identify the evidence, and explain why the passerby is sinful.

Core Idea
Prayer is not invalidated by any passerby, but the passerby commits a grave sin.

A common concern during prayer is whether one's prayer breaks if someone walks in front. The Hanafi school, relying on authentic hadith, clearly rules that the prayer remains valid regardless of the passerby. However, the passerby bears a heavy sin. This lesson examines the proof, the level of dislike, and the cross-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: a person (or animal) passes in front of a praying person. The Hanafi ruling: prayer is not invalidated; the passerby is sinful.
This ruling applies to all passersby: human, animal, etc.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the evidence: the hadith 'لا يقطع الصلاة مرور شيء' (passing does not cut off prayer) and the incident with Aisha (RA).
Both are in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Determine the hukm level for the passerby
From the hadith warning of sin, the dislike is categorized as karaha tahrimiyya (prohibitively disliked).
The explicit mention of sin elevates the level from merely disliked to sinful.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider that certain passersby invalidate prayer. The Hanafi response, based on the explicit hadith and practice, maintains non-invalidation.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in prayer validity.

موضع سجوده كما صرح به الشارح وهو مختار صاحب الهداية وشمس الأئمة السرخسي وقاضيخان، وفي المحيط إنه الأحسن لأن ذلك القدر موضع صلاته دون ما وراءه. وذكر التمرتاشي أن الأصح أنه إن كان بحال لو صلى صلاة خاشع لا يقع بصره على المار فلا يكره المرور نحو «أن يكون منتهى بصره في قيامه إلى موضع سجوده، وفي ركوعه إلى صدور قدميه وفي سجوده إلى أرنبة أنفه، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وفي سلامه إلى منكبيه، واختاره فخر الإسلام فإنه قال : إذا صلى رامياً لوك الشيء بالسن والسن يشمل الثنايا فيمكن أن يلوكه بها كثيراً قوله : (وهو مختار صاحب الهداية) قال الشيخ اسمعيل : فيه نظر فإن قال في الهداية بعد ذكره على ما قيل ا هـ . قلت : As for the third: the passing of a passerby in the place of the prostration of the praying person, it does not invalidate the prayer according to the generality of scholars, whether the passerby is a woman, donkey, dog, or otherwise, due to the hadith in the two Sahihs from Aisha that he was praying while I lay across in front of him, and when he prostrated he nudged me and I pulled back my leg, and when he stood I stretched them out, and the houses at that time had no lamps. And due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The passing of nothing cuts off the prayer, and repel as much as you can, for it is only a devil.' But al-Nawawi declared it weak. In Fath al-Qadir, it appears that it is not less than hasan because it is narrated from multiple chains. Then the discussion on this issue is in seventeen points: First: what the author mentioned in the book of non-invalidation. Second: that the passerby is sinful, due to the hadith: 'If the passerby knew what burden he would bear for passing in front of the praying person, he would prefer to stand for forty...' The narrator said: I do not know if forty years, months, or days. Al-Bazzar narrated it and said: forty autumns. Ibn Majah narrated and Ibn Hibban authenticated from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If any of you knew what he incurs by crossing in front of his brother while he is praying, it would be better for him to stand for a hundred years than to take that step.' And by this it is known that the dislike is tahrimi because they explicitly mention sin, and that is meant by his statement 'and the passerby between his hands is sinful'. Third: concerning the place where passing is disliked, and there is disagreement. The author chose that it is his place of prostration, and he validated it in al-Kafi because this amount of space is his due, and prohibiting beyond it narrows the passersby. This indicates that by 'place of prostration' is meant his place of prayer, from his foot to his place of prostration, as the commentator explicitly stated, and it is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and Qadikhan. In al-Muhit, it is the best because that amount is his place of prayer, not beyond it. Al-Tamartashi mentioned that the correct view is that if he is in a state such that if he prays humbly, his sight does not fall upon the passerby, then passing is not disliked, such that the extent of his sight while standing is to his prostration place, while bowing to the tops of his feet, while prostrating to the tip of his nose, while sitting to his lap, and while saying salam to his shoulders. Fakh al-Islam chose this; he said: if he prays as a marksman... chewing something with the tooth and the tooth includes the incisors, so he can chew it many times. He said: (It is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya) Sheikh Isma'il said: There is consideration in it, for al-Hidaya said after mentioning it 'as was said', end. I say: The explicit statement of the author of al-Nihaya and al-Kifaya that this is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya indicates that it is not a weakening of it, and it seems he brought it to indicate the disagreement. And it indicates that it is his choice because he authenticated it in al-Tajnis as will come shortly. The disagreement referred to is mentioned in al-Fath: among them are those who estimated it as three cubits, some as five, some as forty, and some as... what? (1) Narrated by Bukhari in the book of prayer chapter 101, Muslim in the book of prayer hadith 261, Abu Dawud in the book of prayer chapter 108, Tirmidhi in the book of times chapter 134, Muwatta in the book of travel hadith 34,35, Ahmad in his Musnad 4/169.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling regarding a passerby crossing in front of a person performing prayer. The author begins by stating that the prayer is not invalidated by the passage of anyone, whether a woman, donkey, dog, etc., based on the well-known hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) and the Prophet's statement that passing does not cut off prayer. However, the passerby commits a sin by doing so, as emphasized in another hadith. The passage then details that the dislike (karahah) is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to the explicit mention of sin. It also addresses the location: the place where passing is disliked is the area of the worshipper's prostration, which includes from his feet to his prostration spot, as chosen by many Hanafi authorities. Some scholars, like al-Tamartashi, have a different view based on the worshipper's gaze. The passage ends with a mention of the different estimates of the width of the praying space. This lesson covers the first three of seventeen points mentioned.

Key Terms
مرور المار (murur al-mar): The act of a person walking directly in front of a worshipper during prayer.
كراهة تحريمية (karaha tahrimiyya): Prohibitively disliked; a ruling that is close to haram and involves sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man walks in front of a woman praying, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid
B) The prayer is valid but the passerby is sinful
C) The prayer is valid and the passerby is not sinful because it is a human
D) The prayer is invalid only if the passerby is a woman

Key Takeaway
Prayer is never invalidated by a passerby; the passerby commits a sin (karaha tahrimiyya) by crossing in front of a worshipper.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Disliked Area for Passing in Front of a Worshipper
Clarifying the spatial limit of disliked passing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different Hanafi opinions on the exact area where passing is disliked and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The disliked area is the worshipper's place of prostration from foot to prostration spot; passing beyond that is not sinful.

Once we know that passing in front is sinful, the next question is: where exactly does this apply? Is it the entire area in front of the worshipper or only a specific zone? The Hanafi school has multiple views, with the majority limiting it to the prostration area. This lesson examines those opinions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of contention
The spatial boundary of the disliked area for passing in front of a praying person.
All Hanafi agree that passing in a certain area is sinful, but disagree on its extent.
2
State the majority opinion
The place of prostration: from the worshipper's foot to the prostration spot. This is the choice of al-Hidaya, al-Sarakhsi, Qadikhan, and the author.
The evidence: that area is the worshipper's specific space; prohibiting beyond that would inconvenience people.
3
State the alternative opinion (gaze-based)
Al-Tamartashi and Fakh al-Islam: the disliked area is where the worshipper's sight falls during prayer. If the worshipper prays humbly and does not see the passerby, then passing is not disliked even if within the prostration area.
This view estimates the area based on different postures: standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting.
4
Identify the relied-upon view
The majority view (prostration area) is the one relied upon for fatwa. The author validates it in al-Kafi and considers it the choice of al-Hidaya.
The disagreement on measurements (3 cubits, 5, 40) are secondary and not the operative view.

Source Text

وأما الثالث وهو مرور المار في موضع سجود المصلي فإنما لا يفسدها عند عامة العلماء، سواء كان المار امرأة أو حماراً أو كلباً أو غيرها لحديث الصحيحين عن عائشة أنه كان يصلي وأنا معترضة بين يديه فإذا سجد غمزني فقبضت رجلي فإذا قام بسطتهما والبيوت يومئذ ليس فيها مصابيح، ولقوله عليه السلام لا يقطع الصلاة مرور شيء وادرؤوا ما استطعتم فإنما هو شيطان لكن ضعفه النووي. وفي فتح القدير والذي يظهر أنه لا ينزل عن الحسن لأنه يروى من عدة طرق. ثم الكلام في هذه المسألة في سبعة عشر موضعاً : الأول ما ذكره في الكتاب من عدم الفساد الثاني أن المار آثم للحديث لو يعلم المار بين يدي المصلي ماذا عليه من الوزر لوقف أربعين خير أن يمر بين يديه (١) قال الراوي : لا أدري أربعين عاماً من أو شهراً أو يوماً. وأخرجه البزار وقال : أربعين خريفاً . وروى ابن ماجه وصححه ابن حبان عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لو يعلم أحدكم ما له في أن يمر بين يدي أخيه معترضاً في الصلاة كان لأن يقيم مائة عام خير له من الخطوة التي خطى». وبهذا علم أن الكراهة تحريمية لتصريحهم بالإثم وهو المراد بقوله «وإن أثم المار بين يديه. الثالث في الموضع الذي يكره المرور فيه وفيه اختلاف، واختار المصنف أنه . موضع سجوده، وصححه في الكافي لأن هذا القدر من المكان حقه وفي تحريم ما وراءه تضييق على المارة وهو يفيد أن المراد بموضع سجوده موضع صلاته وهو من قدمه إلى موضع سجوده كما صرح به الشارح وهو مختار صاحب الهداية وشمس الأئمة السرخسي وقاضيخان، وفي المحيط إنه الأحسن لأن ذلك القدر موضع صلاته دون ما وراءه. وذكر التمرتاشي أن الأصح أنه إن كان بحال لو صلى صلاة خاشع لا يقع بصره على المار فلا يكره المرور نحو «أن يكون منتهى بصره في قيامه إلى موضع سجوده، وفي ركوعه إلى صدور قدميه وفي سجوده إلى أرنبة أنفه، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وفي سلامه إلى منكبيه، واختاره فخر الإسلام فإنه قال : إذا صلى رامياً لوك الشيء بالسن والسن يشمل الثنايا فيمكن أن يلوكه بها كثيراً قوله : (وهو مختار صاحب الهداية) قال الشيخ اسمعيل : فيه نظر فإن قال في الهداية بعد ذكره على ما قيل ا هـ . قلت : تصريح صاحب النهاية والكفاية بأن ذلك مختار صاحب الهداية يفيد أن ذلك ليس تضعيفاً له وكأنه أتى به ليشير إلى الخلاف، ويدل على أنه ذلك مختار له تصحيحه له في التجنيس كما سيأتي قريباً. والخلاف المشار إليه كتاب المواقيت باب .١٣٤. الموطأ في كتاب السفر حديث ٣٤، ٣٥. أحمد في مسنده (٤/ ١٦٩).
As for the third: the passing of a passerby in the place of the prostration of the praying person, it does not invalidate the prayer according to the generality of scholars, whether the passerby is a woman, donkey, dog, or otherwise, due to the hadith in the two Sahihs from Aisha that he was praying while I lay across in front of him, and when he prostrated he nudged me and I pulled back my leg, and when he stood I stretched them out, and the houses at that time had no lamps. And due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The passing of nothing cuts off the prayer, and repel as much as you can, for it is only a devil.' But al-Nawawi declared it weak. In Fath al-Qadir, it appears that it is not less than hasan because it is narrated from multiple chains. Then the discussion on this issue is in seventeen points: First: what the author mentioned in the book of non-invalidation. Second: that the passerby is sinful, due to the hadith: 'If the passerby knew what burden he would bear for passing in front of the praying person, he would prefer to stand for forty...' The narrator said: I do not know if forty years, months, or days. Al-Bazzar narrated it and said: forty autumns. Ibn Majah narrated and Ibn Hibban authenticated from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If any of you knew what he incurs by crossing in front of his brother while he is praying, it would be better for him to stand for a hundred years than to take that step.' And by this it is known that the dislike is tahrimi because they explicitly mention sin, and that is meant by his statement 'and the passerby between his hands is sinful'. Third: concerning the place where passing is disliked, and there is disagreement. The author chose that it is his place of prostration, and he validated it in al-Kafi because this amount of space is his due, and prohibiting beyond it narrows the passersby. This indicates that by 'place of prostration' is meant his place of prayer, from his foot to his place of prostration, as the commentator explicitly stated, and it is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and Qadikhan. In al-Muhit, it is the best because that amount is his place of prayer, not beyond it. Al-Tamartashi mentioned that the correct view is that if he is in a state such that if he prays humbly, his sight does not fall upon the passerby, then passing is not disliked, such that the extent of his sight while standing is to his prostration place, while bowing to the tops of his feet, while prostrating to the tip of his nose, while sitting to his lap, and while saying salam to his shoulders. Fakh al-Islam chose this; he said: if he prays as a marksman... chewing something with the tooth and the tooth includes the incisors, so he can chew it many times. He said: (It is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya) Sheikh Isma'il said: There is consideration in it, for al-Hidaya said after mentioning it 'as was said', end. I say: The explicit statement of the author of al-Nihaya and al-Kifaya that this is the choice of the author of al-Hidaya indicates that it is not a weakening of it, and it seems he brought it to indicate the disagreement. And it indicates that it is his choice because he authenticated it in al-Tajnis as will come shortly. The disagreement referred to is mentioned in al-Fath: among them are those who estimated it as three cubits, some as five, some as forty, and some as... what? Key Terms

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Hidayah, the disliked area for passing in front of a worshipper is:
A) Within three cubits
B) The place of prostration from foot to prostration spot
C) The entire range of the worshipper's sight
D) Only directly in front of the nose

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi position is that passing is disliked only in the prostration area (foot to prostration spot); passing beyond is not sinful.
